---||World||India's investment seems sinking in Afghanistan, warns Pakistan army||ISLAMABAD: Pakistan Army spokesperson Major General Babar Iftikhar claimed on Saturday that India‚Äôs investments in Afghanistan seemed to be "sinking" and added that "Indian propaganda" against Pakistan and its role in the peace process was "not gaining traction". New Delhi and Kabul share deepened economic and trade links despite uncertainties about achieving a political settlement to the lingering conflict in Afghanistan. India has invested over $3 billion in reconstruction and relief work since 2001 when US-led troops drove the Taliban out of Kabul. Delhi still firmly supports President Ashraf Ghani‚Äôs government. In an interview with a local TV channel, Gen Iftikhar said that "spoilers" (an indirect reference to India) were trying to hold Pakistan responsible for the deteriorating situation in Afghanistan prompted by the announcements of withdrawal of US and Nato forces from the war-torn country. "But there is no truth is these allegations. The world is very well aware that Pakistan has made every effort to solve the Afghan issue, without violence and according to the wishes of the Afghan people," the military spokesperson said. "Pakistan is still a facilitator of this peace process and not a guarantor," the general said. Responding to a question about whether the US should remove itself completely from the region, he said there was only one requirement from the US: a responsible withdrawal from Afghanistan. "What that meant was their exit would have happened after a transition. But it happened a little quickly. I think that it has been said with a lot of clarity that there is no question nor requirement of bases for the US," Gen Iftikhar said, adding that the regional powers were well capable of resolving the issue. "So you are saying the Americans are not needed, that they can leave?" the interviewer asked. "No, I don‚Äôt think they are needed," he replied. When asked about the perception in Afghanistan that the Taliban would come to power, he said: "We need to understand that if that happens, that would be the decision of the Afghans. No one will dictate this decision from the outside."||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//world/pakistan/indias-investment-seems-sinking-in-afghanistan-warns-pakistan-army/articleshow/84303562.cms||Omer Farooq Khan

---||Bengaluru||Karnataka: Five years on, paperless legislature plan remains on paper||BENGALURU: In the pipeline for over a decade, the proposal to make the state legislature paperless remains a non-starter. Five years ago, Karnataka had revived the project and entered into an agreement with the Centre over the cost-sharing mechanism to implement the national eVidhan project. The Centre and the state had agreed to share the cost (Rs 69 crore) under a 60:40 ratio. But nothing has moved thereafter. ‚ÄúFrom software customisations to a lack of political will, the state government hasn‚Äôt taken any step to implement the system which is currently operating in 16 other states,‚Äô‚Äô secretariat officials said. And it is unlikely to be implemented anytime soon, as the government has asked legislature officials to do a gap analysis between what Karnataka requires and what is being implemented in other states. Chief secretary P Ravi Kumar told STOI directions have been given for the gap analysis and submit a report in a month. ‚ÄúWhile we admit there has been a delay, it has not been easy as well. There have been concerns with regard to customising the software to our needs,‚Äù he said. Software glitchesAccording to government officials, trouble began soon after Karnataka legislature proposed to go paperless 2015-16. It took a leaf out of Himachal Pradesh‚Äôs software implementation called National e-Vidhan Application (NeVa). ‚ÄúHowever, it was found that NeVa could be applied only to unicameral legislatures and till date only those states have implemented the system,‚Äù said an official. While Karnataka still has the option to ditch the software and get its own customised and local application for going paperless, the government appears to be keen on the central government funding. ‚ÄúWhile we‚Äôre exploring options, NeVa software implementation would mean the Centre will provide 60 per cent of the funding,‚Äù said Ravi Kumar. According to officials, the Centre has allocated Rs 250 crore towards implementing the NeVa project nationwide and could provide additional funding if required. But the biggest stumbling block has been the lack of political will. ‚ÄúWhen senior leaders are not keen on embracing technology then there is nothing you can do,‚Äù said a senior BJP MLA.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/bengaluru/5-yrs-on-paperless-legislature-plan-remains-on-paper/articleshow/84303674.cms||Sandeep Moudgal
---||Bengaluru||Bangalore Water Supply and Sewerage Board mulls 5% discount on water bills for bldgs with RWH||BENGALURU: The Bangalore Water Supply and Sewerage Board (BWSSB) is contemplating taking the reward route to popularise implementation of rainwater harvesting: It may give 5 per cent discount on monthly water bills to properties with RWH facilities. The idea was brainstormed on Saturday during a virtual session titled ‚ÄòCatch the Rain, Bengaluru‚Äô organised by National Water Mission, BWSSB and Biome Environmental. The rebate on water bill, if offered, will be on the lines of the concession being extended by BBMP on property tax paid before the due date, and is expected to encourage more property owners to install RWH systems. National Water Mission director G Asok Kumar mooted the idea and BWSSB chairman N Jayaram responded, stating the proposal will be taken up for discussion at the next board meeting. BWSSB till now provides an appreciation certificate to those implementing RWH. Jayaram said, ‚ÄúBBMP provides 5% rebate on property tax if it is paid early in the financial year and in the same way, we could also see what can be done to promote RWH.‚Äù While Bengaluru‚Äôs dependence on Cauvery river and other sources for water has resulted in losses for BWSSB, Jayaram said RWH can really help the city. Giving an example, he said it takes Rs 95 to supply 1,000 litres of Cauvery water to Bengaluru, while only Rs seven is collected from citizens for the same. He added exponential growth of the city will pose a challenge if RWH is not implemented with citizens‚Äô active participation. According to Jayaram, Cauvery water is brought to the city from 90km away. About 1,440MLD is being supplied to Bengaluru and additional ground water of 600 MLD is drawn. BM Somashekar, chief engineer of the board, said despite the number of rainy days having come down in the city, Bengaluru continues to receive 850mm rainfall annually. But very little is being saved and reused. The board has brought in many awareness programmes to promote RWH, including taking citizens and students to Sir M Visvesvaraya Rain Water Harvesting Theme Park. According to BWSSB, Bengaluru spans about 800sqkm, but BWSSB jurisdiction is 570sqkm as of now, serving a population of 80.5 lakh, while others continue to depend on water tankers, especially those living in apartments. Average per capita consumption of water in Bengaluru is about 65 lakh litres a day. Somashekar said BWSSB has about 8,000 active borewells in the city, but many are drying up during summer. He added they have about 27 RWH models for citizens, which can not only help them reuse water but recharge borewells too. Kumar said training plumbers can make a big difference. Some residents who have implemented RWH shared their experiences, saying how they don‚Äôt have to rely on water tankers and BWSSB. Ashok Mrityunjaya, a resident of Aditi Elite apartment in Bellandur, said the complex did not have a BWSSB connection and was dependent on tankers. But after implementing RWH and digging borewells to recharge water, they have been able to sustain for almost one year.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/bengaluru/bwssb-mulls-5-discount-onwater-bills-for-bldgs-with-rwh/articleshow/84303712.cms||Kiran Parashar

The challenge before Karnataka is to get necessary clearances from various ministries and agencies of the central government. The Mekedatu balancing reservoir-cum-drinking water project which seeks to alleviate drinking water needs of Bengaluru and Ramanagara districts besides generating upto 400MW of electricity has been awaiting clearances for four years owing to opposition by neighbouring Tamil Nadu. Karnataka is also awaiting Central Water Commission‚Äôs approval for the detailed project report (DPR) on Mekedatu and environmental nod from the Union ministry of forest, environment and ecology to take up the project. In 2018, the state got nod from the Union water resources ministry for preparation of DPR amid stiff opposition from TN. ‚ÄúThe draft DPR is currently under consideration of CWC. It is a long-drawn process as has to go through several departments. Once we get the approval, the government will start work on implementation,‚Äù said Rakesh Singh, additional chief secretary, water resources department. The government also needs environmental clearance as over 5,050 hectares of forest land, including 3,180 acres of Cauvery wildlife sanctuary, will be submerged due the project. It was originally planned as just a hydel power project three decades ago, but was modified keeping the drinking water needs of Bengaluru city in mind. The project got a boost after the Supreme Court allowed Karnataka to utilise additional 4.8 tmcft of Cauvery water to meet Bengaluru‚Äôs drinking water needs. Another reason for the modification is to hold excess water that flows into the sea so that both Karnataka and Tamil Nadu can utilise it during distress years. According to an estimation, around 200 tmcft of water flows into the sea during excess monsoon rain. But Tamil Nadu claims the project will jeopardise the availability of Cauvery water for TN. Karnataka, however, feel Tamil Nadu‚Äôs apprehensions are uncalled for. Last week, Yediyurappa tried to get his TN counterpart MK Stalin to take part in bilateral talks to find an amicable solution. But Stalin flatly rejected the offer and suggested Karnataka scrap the project. ‚ÄòState needn‚Äôt take TN consent‚Äô‚ÄúKarnataka needn‚Äôt have to take the TN government‚Äôs consent. Since we are utilising water that is allocated to us, the government must go ahead and implement the project. The government must put pressure on the Centre to get necessary approvals as early as possible,‚Äù said Brijesh Kalappa, a Congress functionary and advocate, who was part of the Karnataka legal team on water disputes. Kalappa claimed Yediyurappa‚Äôs decision to write to the TN CM was ill-advised. Now all eyes will be on the all-party meeting in Chennai on Monday convened by Stalin to hold a discussion regarding Mekedatu dam construction.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/bengaluru/karnataka-still-awaits-cwc-green-clearance-for-mekedatu/articleshow/84303715.cms||Anil Gejji

---||Bengaluru||Karnataka: Alert in districts to check Zika spread||BENGALURU: The health department has directed all districts to put in place vector-management plans to prevent outbreak of Zika virus cases which have been reported in neighbouring Kerala. In his order on Saturday, health and family welfare commissioner KV Thrilok Chandra asked all district administrations to ensure ASHA workers and health assistance monitor regularly in rural areas and fortnightly in urban wards. The department asked officials of Chamarajanagar, Dakshina Kannada and Udupi districts in particular to be more vigilant. Monsoon tends to facilitate the spread of Aedes mosquito, which is a vector for Zika virus. Solid waste needs to be effectively disposed of to prevent its breeding. Vector-borne disease control officers of all 31 districts need to step up mid-term strategies, the circular said. Vigil should be stepped up in public places like airports, ports and harbours. The travel history of visitors and even guests at home need to be checked and their samples taken, if needed. They must be sent to National Institute of Virology, Bengaluru, the circular added. The department directed officials to ensure availability of adulticide and larvicide, used for killing mosquitoes, and hold regular inter-sectoral meetings to help in exchange of information.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/bengaluru/alert-in-dists-to-check-zika-spread/articleshow/84303995.cms||---

In January 2021, BMRCL terminated the contract of Simplex Infrastructures Limited over delayed execution of work on the 7.5-km section between Kalena Agrahara (Gottigere) and Tavarekere (Swagath Road Cross). In March 2021, a fresh tender was floated. ---||India||After many false starts, IMD says monsoon set to hit Delhi today||NEW DELHI: Reeling under scorching heat and high humidity, Delhi-NCR residents may finally get some rain relief. The Met department says the long-delayed monsoon is likely to hit the region on Sunday, bringing some showers in its wake that would lower temperatures over the next few days. However, Delhiites will be wary. So far, the monsoon has repeatedly failed to keep its ‚Äî rather, the India Meteorological Department‚Äôs ‚Äî dates with the capital. The IMD had initially forecast the monsoon‚Äôs arrival around mid-June, which would have made it one of the earliest onsets over Delhi. The next likely onset window, July first week, too went by with no signs of the rain-bearing system. If the monsoon finally hits the city on Sunday, it would be the most delayed advent in 19 years. Only light rain likely for next 4 daysDelhi had last seen a more delayed monsoon onset in 2002, when it reached the city on July 19. On Saturday, the Met department said Delhi is expected to see the onset of the southwest monsoon by Sunday, forecasting its progress over Delhi, west Uttar Pradesh, Punjab, Haryana and Rajasthan in the next 24 hours. While the IMD had initially forecast light rains over Delhi on Saturday and moderate showers from Sunday onwards, it said the intensity of the expected rain had reduced, with only light rainfall likely from Sunday until Wednesday. ‚ÄúLower level easterly winds from the Bay of Bengal have further extended northwestward, reaching up to Delhi, Haryana and east Rajasthan, as on today,‚Äù the IMD said on Saturday in its daily monsoon bulletin, adding that conditions were favourable for ‚Äúfurther advancement of the southwest monsoon over Delhi, remaining parts of West Uttar Pradesh, some more parts of Punjab, Haryana and Rajasthan during the next 24 hours‚Äù. ‚ÄúConditions are also becoming favourable for further advancement of the southwest monsoon over the remaining parts of the country, during the subsequent 48 hours,‚Äù it added. R K Jenamani, scientist at IMD, said some parts of the city may receive isolated spells of very light rain on Saturday night, however, there were greater chances of rain on Sunday, with rain activity expected in the afternoon and evening. ‚ÄúIt is expected to progress into Delhi in the next 24 hours and the onset will be declared based on when Delhi gets covered completely,‚Äù said Jenamani. Since July 1, the IMD had been forecasting that monsoon was likely to hit Delhi by July 10. It‚Äôs initial forecast of an early onset (mid-June) was thwarted by the monsoon weakening literally at the doorstep of Delhi-NCR. The normal date for onset of the monsoon in Delhi is June 27. Last year, it hit the city two days early, on June 25. The capital recorded a maximum temperature of 39.8 degrees Celsius on Saturday at Safdarjung, Delhi‚Äôs base station. This was four degrees above normal. Humidity levels too remained high, oscillating between 46% and 77%. Najafgarh was the warmest location in Delhi, with the maximum at 40.7 degrees Celsius, IMD data showed. With monsoon playing hooky and scalding westerly winds blowing for several days, the city has had six 40-degree-plus days in July already. Last year, July saw just one such day while 2019 and 2018 had two each. However, with the monsoon predicted to finally arrive, the Met office said Sunday‚Äôs maximum is likely to drop to 35 degrees C, which could further dip to 32 degrees C by Tuesday.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//india/after-many-false-starts-imd-says-monsoon-set-to-hit-delhi-today/articleshow/84305626.cms||---

---||India||A retired SC judge can get paid more in 2 hours than a serving one in a month||NEW DELHI: If there is a travesty about the principle of equal work, equal pay, one need not turn to the urban-hinterland disparity as a comparison of compensation paid to a Supreme Court judge for hearing and deciding a case and to a senior advocate for arguing it brings out the wide chasm. An SC judge gets a salary of Rs 2.5 lakh a month, which works out to approximately Rs 8,333 per day, during which he hears arguments from lawyers on an average in 40 cases. This translates to Rs 208 per case, be it a simple appeal, a PIL on Covid issues, or one involving intricate questions of law. In contrast, a newly designated senior advocate commands a price of Rs 1 lakh to Rs 5 lakh for arguing a case. The services of a seasoned advocate like A M Singhvi, Kapil Sibal, Mukul Rohatgi or Harish Salve may find the litigant's bank balance lighter by Rs 10 lakh-20 lakh per hearing. So an SC judge, who hears and decides a case, gets Rs 208 per day per case while seasoned senior advocates, who cannot guarantee a result in a case, are paid in lakhs of rupees per day per case. Well, none of the senior advocates argue in 40 cases a day, for which an SC judge prepares every evening to be ready to listen to the legal arguments the next day. This is the reason why many SC judges look forward to their retirement, which allows them to offer legal expertise as arbitrators, or, for that matter, provide valued opinion to corporations and multinationals on legal issues in their operations in India, or in disputes arising from contracts, agreements and MoUs. A retired SC judge earns between Rs 2 lakh and Rs 5 lakh for a two-hour sitting as an arbitrator and there are some who do three sittings every day to match the earnings of a reasonably successful senior advocate. A retired Chief Justice of India commands a little more than a retired SC judge while performing the duty of an arbitrator. In rendering an opinion, a retired SC judge gets between Rs 5 lakh and Rs 10 lakh while each opinion of a retired CJI fetches her/him Rs 10-20 lakh. A retired CJI confided to TOI: "I do three to four opinions a month and earn between Rs 30-50 lakh, unthinkable money for a sitting judge. I indulge in a lot of charity. And yet, I am left with an amount which is more than the provident fund money I got on retirement after rendering services for more than two decades as a judge of constitutional courts." The only difference between a senior advocate and an SC judge, in terms of compensation, is the sprawling Lutyens‚Äô Zone bungalow and free services of assistants that s/he is entitled to. Some of the bungalows allotted to SC judges are built on two acres of land. A future CJI, in a candid conversation, said, "The benefits and perquisites given to judges are far better than those provided in the 1980s. There was no individual vehicle given to SC judges then. But now the facilities are comparable to those availed by such judges of other countries. The salary is low but the facilities make up for it."||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//india/a-retired-sc-judge-can-get-paid-more-in-2-hours-than-a-serving-one-in-a-month/articleshow/84307245.cms||Dhananjay Mahapatra

A wide network of functioning primary health centres and health workers experienced in mass vaccination programmes such as against polio helped pace up the vaccination. ‚ÄúCovid vaccination was nothing new for our grassroots health workers experienced in programmes such as for polio. It was just another programme to be implemented,‚Äù the official said requesting anonymity. ---||Mysuru||Monsoon revs up: Heavy rain in Karnataka till July 15||BENGALURU: After a lull in end-June and early July, monsoon has picked up in the state, much to the relief of farmers. The Met office has forecast heavy to extremely heavy rain across the state over the next five days. Thundershowers are likely in Bengaluru in the next 48 hours. The state received 198mm of rain through June, against a normal of 199mm. The dry spell was between June 18 and July 8. Since then, heavy rain has been lashing coastal and Malnad districts and parts of North Karnataka. From June 1 to July 10, the state received 246mm rain against the normal of 284mm. Red alert issued in DK, Udupi, Uttara KannadaThe Karnataka State Natural Disaster Monitoring Centre (KSNDMC) has issued a red alert, warning of heavy rain in Dakshina Kannada, Udupi and Uttara Kannada districts on Sunday. An orange alert was sounded in Chikkamagaluru, Hassan, Kodagu and Shivamogga districts and yellow alert in Chamarajanagar, Mandya, Mysuru, Ramanagara, Kalaburagi, Vijayapura, Bagalkot, Bidar, Belagavi, Dharwad, Gadag and Haveri districts. ‚ÄúThe strengthening of south-westerly winds from Arabian Sea and likely formation of a low-pressure area over west central and adjoining northwest Bay of Bengal will result in active monsoon conditions with enhanced rainfall activity in various parts of the state,‚Äù said Manoj Rajan, commissioner, KSNDMC. He said for the remaining duration of southwest monsoon (till end of September), the state is likely to see normal to above-normal rain. Dam storage goodThe storage at 13 major damsin Karnataka is good. ‚ÄúThe total storage is about 332 tmc ft (44%) of the total gross capacity of 860 tmc ft as on Saturday, when compared to 322 tmc ft (38%) of the total capacity last year,‚Äô‚Äô said Rajan.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/mysuru/monsoon-revs-up-heavyrain-in-state-till-july-15/articleshow/84312287.cms||---

---||India||Record 354kg heroin worth Rs 2,500 crore seized by Delhi cops||NEW DELHI: In the biggest drug bust in its history, Delhi Police's special cell has seized 354kg of grade A heroin worth a staggering Rs 2,500 crore in the international market. Four key members of a cartel, including a chemical expert who turned crude powder into pure heroin, have been arrested. The network is spread across several countries with kingpins based in Canada, Portugal and Afghanistan and multiple modules are active in India to carry out narco-terrorism activities in the country, the cops said. The cartel, investigations have revealed, was importing under the cover of legitimate goods like talc stone, gypsum powder and basil seeds, packed in material like gunny bags, cartons etc. It was then transported in containers to Iran‚Äôs Chabahar port. "From there, the consignments containing the contraband were shipped to Jawaharlal Nehru Port Trust, Mumbai. Thereafter, the material was separated from the legitimate consignments and sent to makeshift factories," DCP (special cell) Pramod Kushwaha told TOI. Special chemical experts from Afghanistan were then roped in to process the contraband and turn it into pure and saleable heroin. One such processor, Hazrat Ali from Kandahar, is among those arrested. His associate, Rizwan Kashmiri from Anantnag, has been arrested as well apart from two members of the Punjab wing of this cartel. About 100kg of the chemical used to turn crude contraband into pure heroin has also been seized. The operation was conducted by ACPs Lalit Mohan Negi and Hriday Bhushan from the New Delhi range of the cell. The team had busted a similar module in 2019. Developing leads which had stemmed from that operation, ACP Negi learned that a suspect named Rizwan was dealing in drugs across Delhi and Madhya Pradesh. On July 5, specific information was received about Rizwan's movements in Ghitorni area of south Delhi. Inspector Vinod Badola, SI Sundar Gautam and others laid a trap and arrested the suspect with 1kg of heroin. However, this turned out to be just the tip of the iceberg. During interrogation, Kashmiri allegedly revealed that he worked under the command of an Afghan national, Isha Khan, who recently left India and is now based in Afghanistan. Khan had directed Kashmiri to contact two men, Gurpreet Singh and Gurjot Singh, both residents of Punjab, who were operating a drug racket from NSG Vihar Coop Housing Society in Sector 65, Faridabad. A raid was conducted and both were apprehended. The two led the cops to two cars ‚Äî Verna and Amaze ‚Äî having 166kg and 115kg of heroin, respectively. Further, 70kg of the substance was seized from the bed box of their flat, leaving the cops stunned over the scale of recovery. The two men have claimed that they work for a Portugal-based handler named Navpreet Singh. Gurpreet had met him when the two were lodged in Kapurthala jail in a drugs case. Navpreet works in coordination with his counterparts in Afghanistan, Iran and Canada. Meanwhile, based on Rizwan's disclosure, the cops arrested Hazrat Ali and seized chemicals and heroin from him as well. Ali and others were part of the chemical module of this syndicate and were operating from makeshift factories in different states, the biggest of them being in Shivpuri, Madhya Pradesh, at present. "The locals, with the help of Afghan experts, process the heroin and the various chemicals required for this are procured by the network members from various chemical shops located in MP and Delhi. After preparation, the heroin is delivered to Punjab, Delhi, Haryana, Rajasthan J&K and various other parts of India using different supply chains," DCP Kushwaha said. The arrested people are parts of different components of this network. This module is suspected to be part of a bigger network. Police commissioner Balaji Srivastava is learned to have formed a special team to unearth the entire nexus. Efforts are on to track the source based in Afghanistan in coordination with intelligence agencies apart from tracing conduits active at the Mumbai port and others parts of the country.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//india/record-354kg-heroin-worth-rs-2500-crore-seized-by-delhi-cops/articleshow/84307678.cms||Raj Sekhar

---||Ahmedabad||Aadhaar‚Äôs catch-22: To get missing man‚Äôs information, trace him!||AHMEDABAD: A 19-year-old boy, Jigar Jadav, went missing from his school in Devas village in Banaskantha in 2011. A decade later, when the local police sought help from the Unique Identification Authority of India (UIDAI) to provide any and every available detail on Jadav to help trace him, the Aadhaar authority cited the right to privacy of the person--missing in this case. In March this year, the Gujarat HC directed Banaskantha police to launch an investigation to trace Jadav and ordered UIDAI to cooperate with the police to trace Jadav through Aadhaar card, if it was issued at all to him. Reluctant to share Aadhaar information, if it has any, on missing Jadav, the UIDAI authorities informed the Gujarat high court that the HC can order it to furnish information only after hearing the authority and the person whose information is being sought for. Ironically, in this case, it is a missing person! The insistence on part of the Aadhaar authority on following the law perplexed the HC which directed UIDAI on Wednesday to cooperate with the police in its investigation into the disappearance of Jadav after 10 years following a habeas corpus petition filed by Jadav‚Äôs father, Nagjibhai. Jadav had disappeared from Dr Babasaheb Ambedkar Kumar Chhatralay in Devas village in Banaskantha. His father frantically inquired with the schools and hostel authorities and pursued the matter with high-ups in the government. When no trace of his son was found, he approached the high court through advocate Nayanavati Jethva. Following the HC order, the Deesa police wrote to UIDAI seeking information about Jadav, if it has any. In reply, the authority said that it would be difficult to identify a person merely on the basis of his birth date and name and without Aadhaar number. The authority later reiterated this in its affidavit filed in the high court and asserted that it would not be feasible to trace him on the basis of cursory details. It also cited various provisions of laws and court orders by which the right to privacy restricts disclosure of details pertaining to an Aadhaar card holder. The Aadhaar authority further submitted that the court can order it to furnish information about an Aadhaar card holder only after hearing UIDAI and the person concerned. It cited provisions of section 33(1) of UIDAI Act. ‚ÄúIt is pertinent to mention that since Mr. Jigar Kumar Nagji Bhai Jadav has now attained majority (as per the information provided by state police authorities), he is also required to be heard by the Court along with the authority in view of the aforesaid Section 33 (1) of the said Act (as amended), in case if he has enrolled himself for an Aadhaar number and subsequently allotted the same by the Authority,‚Äù the affidavit reads. Meanwhile, the Banaskantha police submitted its report on the probe during the hearing. The HC has posted the matter for further hearing on July 26.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/ahmedabad/aadhaars-catch-22-to-get-missing-mans-info-trace-him/articleshow/84304671.cms||Saeed Khan

---||Visakhapatnam||Low pressure likely to form over Bay of Bengal off north Andhra Pradesh coast||VISAKHAPATNAM: The India Meteorological Department (IMD) on Saturday said that a cyclonic circulation lies over coastal Odisha and its neighbourhood between 2.1 and 3.6 km above the mean sea level. Under the influence of the cyclonic circulation, a low pressure area is likely to form over west-central and the adjoining northwest Bay of Bengal off the north Andhra Pradesh and south Odisha coasts by Sunday. The IMD officials said that the low pressure will active the southwest monsoon in Andhra Pradesh and some other states in north India and bring rainfall. The IMD also predicted that thunderstorms to moderate rains are very likely over many parts of north Andhra Pradesh and heavy rain is likely at a few places on Sunday and Monday. The rains will be accompanied by gales with speeds of 40 to 60 kmph in coastal areas. Similarly, in coastal Andhra Pradesh, moderate rainfall is likely in some places and heavy rain is likely in some places on Sunday and Monday. The Rayalaseema region will witness light to moderate and heavy rains in isolated places on Monday.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/visakhapatnam/low-pressure-area-likely-to-form-over-bay/articleshow/84302495.cms||---

---||Goa||Abhilash Tomy ready to cast off again, starts crowdfunding for golden globe race||PANAJI: Undeterred by the horrific accident in 2018 that left him with two spinal fractures, former naval officer Abhilash Tomy is ready to cast off for another shot at circumnavigating the Earth alone. Determined to compete in the 2022 edition of the Golden Globe Race (GGR), a solo non-stop circumnavigation without satellite-based navigation aids, the decorated sailor is looking to crowdfund his race. For some, the relentless desire to sail alone for 60,000km through unforgiving seas and unpredictable Nature best describes a daredevil, but for the former naval commander, it is nothing short of a spiritual journey of self discovery. ‚ÄúI believe that you cannot explore your self if you don‚Äôt cut yourself off from this world. When you are with people, you are always dealing with the external world. Being alone for a prolonged duration kind of alters my mind and I get to know myself,‚Äù said Tomy while speaking to TOI. However, before he gets down to his unfinished business with the South Indian Ocean, Tomy has to figure out the part of his puzzle; funds. For a good competitive race, he will need around Rs 4 crore, but he knows that this may be a tough ask through crowdfunding. He has also reached out to corporate sponsors but has yet to hear anything concrete. His online campaign (https://bit.ly/3k2ifW6)has raised Rs 3.5 lakh. ‚ÄúFor me it is very simple, get a boat, do a 2,000-mile training on it, get it ready and I am set,‚Äù said Tomy, who has settled in Goa with his family. This time around, he is not building a boat since it entails a lot of time, money and compliance. Instead, he plans to purchase a pre-owned boat from Europe and refit it for the race. While his earlier 32-foot yacht, the Thuriya, was a two-masted boat, Tomy has set his eyes on a couple of single-masted 36-footer yachts. Forced out of the Golden Globe Race in 2018 after a severe storm wrecked his yacht and left him injured in one of the remotest parts of the Southern Indian Ocean, the Kirti Chakra winner says he has unfinished business with the oceans. A massive multinational rescue mission helped rescue Tomy who now has titanium rods inserted into his spine. The former naval aviator, who retired from the Indian Navy in January, is candid when he says that out at sea is where he belongs. During his first solo circumnavigation, Tomy began to struggle with the idea of returning to shore after crossing Cape Horn. ‚ÄúI think for anybody to survive through prolonged solitude, where every moment you are worried whether you will survive, you need to have some sort of philosophical strength. In my first circumnavigation, I had to train myself to get back to land,‚Äù said Tomy. He also believes that a nation that looks to the sea, which ventures out and imbibes the maritime spirit can change its ethos. ‚ÄúIf a generation of Indians go out to sea, we will be a completely different nation. Sailing nations such as the Netherlands are the best example. You are honest, helpful, you value time, you learn a lot of skills and it gives you patience. And when you come on land, the small problems stop bothering you. Going to sea helps in character development,‚Äù said Tomy. The 1968 Golden Globe was the first ever around the world yacht race. Open to sailors young and old, it is affordable in 32-36ft strong, recycled, seaworthy yet simple yachts which lack technology, satellite communications and GPS and autopilot systems. The 2022 edition has already received around 30 entrants from 11 countries.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/goa/tomy-ready-to-cast-off-again-starts-crowdfunding-to-raise-funds-for-race/articleshow/84306077.cms||Newton Sequeira

---||Visakhapatnam||VMRDA draft plan flags need to save critical natural assets||VISAKHAPATNAM: The Visakhapatnam Metropolitan Region Development Authority (VMRDA) draft master plan-2041 has proposed a 10-point strategy to protect the critical environment in the VMRDA region. Close to 20% of the VMRDA area (or 1,230 square kilometres) is a natural and sensitive area, which requires protection and integration into the human landscape to retain its environmental significance. The VMRDA area covers a coastal length of 250 km. At present, the total land use covered by recreation, forest and hills constitutes a total green coverage of 12% of VMRDA area. If the plantation around lakes and rivers is considered, this becomes a green cover of 17%, which is much lower than the state and national average. However, this green cover still acts as the backbone for the ecological footprint of the region. Other natural features include coastal sandy areas, mangrove forests, rivers, water bodies and open spaces. Different environmental features also add to the sensitivity of the region towards large-scale developments. As per the draft master plan-2041 framework for environmental management of key sensitive areas, the entire VMRDA is broadly classified into six key designations for its environmental sustainability, protection and conservation. The areas are divided based on characteristics, physiography and natural resources. Each zone will have its own development and protection policy, and maintaining it will facilitate a better environment and healthy surroundings in the VMRDA. The draft master plan also highlights dwindling water resources. Apart from the continuous drought and deficit rainfall prevailing in the last few years, developments and habitations in the catchment area have blocked inflows into water bodies. Meanwhile, coastal areas in the region are subject to intense development pressures by way of tourism, marine fishing activity and industrial infrastructure. In a bid to implement the conservation and protection strategy, the master plan does not propose intensive land uses along the coast other than such permitted under the Coastal Regulation Zone Notification 2011 and subsequent amendments. No other activity, not ancillary to the fishing activity or any conservation activity, has been proposed as part of the coastal areas. The draft master plan also recommends protecting all lakes, lakefronts and all critical channels of lakes through mandatory open and green buffers.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/visakhapatnam/vmrda-draft-plan-flags-need-to-save-critical-natural-assets/articleshow/84302297.cms||Umamaheswara Rao

---||Ahmedabad||Gujarat close to achieving its target of enrolling 10,000 foreign students||AHMEDABAD: Gujarat may achieve its target of enrolling 10,000 foreign students in colleges offering technical courses in the next few months, well ahead of the 2022 deadline. So far, about 8,916 applications have been received from overseas students in over 15 universities, including state government run and self-financed institutions, said sources in the Gujarat government. ‚ÄúAdmissions of 3,111 students have already been confirmed and soon the government will enrol others after proper verification,‚Äù said a senior government official. Gujarat University (GU) has received the highest number of applications, at 2,660, so far for technical courses in various colleges affiliated to it. GU has confirmed the admissions of 1,030 students, said sources. Gujarat Technological University has admitted 809 foreign students; it had received 1,240 applications. MSU in Vadodara has enrolled 541 of the 852 candidates who had applied. Marwadi University, a private institution in Rajkot, got 1,256 applications and 47 students have been given admissions so far, said government sources. National Forensic Sciences University in the state capital of Gandhinagar, which is an Institution of National Importance, has confirmed admissions for 170 candidates of the 315 applications received. It is the world‚Äôs first and only university dedicated to forensics, cybersecurity, digital forensics, and allied sciences. Others such as Swarnim Startup University, Pandit Deendayal Energy University, and Charusat University have confirmed the intake of one, seven, and four foreign candidates respectively. Pandit Deendayal Energy University has received 572 applications from foreign students, said sources. Veer Narmad South Gujarat University has confirmed admissions for 152 foreign candidates of the 276 applicants. The Gujarat government had passed the Gujarat Professional Technical Educational Colleges or Institutions (Regulation of Admission and Fixation of Fees) Bill, 2019. It changed an earlier law that allowed only private colleges to admit students from other places. The new set of rules gives room to foreign students to get admission in any college or institution in the state. The new rules also aimed to reduce the number of government-reserved seats for professional courses and open direct admissions to foreign nationals and students from other Indian states to study in Gujarat. A large number of seats in technical courses remain vacant in the state. ‚ÄúIt seems that the number of candidates wanting to do professional courses is small compared to the total number of approved seats in Gujarat,‚Äù said a government official familiar with the matter. ‚ÄúHence, more than 50% of the seats of self-financed institutions remain vacant after the intake process is carried out by the Admission Committee for Professional Courses (ACPC).‚Äù States such as Maharashtra, Tamil Nadu, and Karnataka capture a large share of foreign students coming to India to pursue higher studies. Gujarat plans to follow a similar path, the official added. According to the new rules, the government-reserved seats in unaided or self-financed colleges have been reduced from 75% to 50%. Also, management-quota seats have been raised from 25% to 50%. This includes 15% non-resident Indian seats, and seats for foreign students and students from any state (including Gujarat).||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/ahmedabad/state-close-to-10000-foreign-students-target/articleshow/84305608.cms||Bharat Yagnik

---||Pune||Covid-19: At 0.9%, weekly case fatality rate of Pune district drops to 70-day low||PUNE: The weekly Covid-19 Case Fatality Rate (CFR) dropped to a 70-day low of 0.9% during the July 1-7 period in the district, health department data revealed. The district‚Äôs weekly CFR had increased to 1.5% in the first week of May. It rose to 2.3% during the week ending May 19 and kept on increasing ever since during the consequent weeks to 2.7%, followed by 2.9% from May 27 to June 2 and 3% during the June 3-9 period, the health department data revealed. The easing in the CFR started in the second week of June when it fell to 1.8% in the week ending June 16. This was the first time that the case fatality rate went below 2% in the 40 days. The latest week, July 1-7, saw a further drop in CFR to 0.9%. The number of weekly Covid deaths in Pune district during the July 1-7 period dropped more than three-fold in comparison to those recorded during the first few days of June, the data showed. The number of positive cases totalled to 8,204 in the July 1-7 period, a slight rise from the preceding week (June 24-30). However, the number of Covid deaths recorded was 80 in the latest week (July 1-7) as against 120 during the week before. Dr Sanjay Deshmukh, assistant director (medical), Pune circle, told TOI, ‚ÄúCovid death rate begins falling almost two to three weeks after the number of cases starts dropping. Covid cases started declining in the first week of June, and the death rate started coming down from the second fortnight of the month. In conjunction with this trend, hospital ICU and oxygen beds are also seeing relatively less Covid admissions now.‚Äù ‚Äú However, Pune‚Äôs weekly positivity rate has remained static (around 6%) during the past few weeks,‚Äù Deshmukh said. He said positivity was not dropping because of the easing of restrictions to an extent, lack of adherence to Covid-appropriate behaviour like wearing masks and people‚Äôs inflow to Pune from districts, such as Kolhapur, Satara and Sangli, which are witnessing high positivity rate. Dr Jitendra Oswal, deputy medical director at Bharati Hospital, said, ‚ÄúThe number of Covid admissions in hospitals has remained static since the past month. As the number of Covid patients is few, the deaths are less too. The number of backlog Covid cases, such as those who are serious and admitted to ICUs, is also currently less. A chunk of backlog cases (patients staying in hospitals for a prolonged period) has now cleared. The number of critical cases, which would be over 1,000 at a time in a hospital, has now dropped to 150-200. Referrals of critical patients from other districts to Pune have also significantly decreased in the last week or so.‚Äù||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/pune/at-0-9-punes-cfr-drops-to-70-day-low/articleshow/84305603.cms||Neha Madaan

---||Ahmedabad||Gujarat: 70% of last year‚Äôs organ donation level achieved||AHMEDABAD: In the past one and a half months, the state recorded more than seven donations of organs retrieved from cadavers. Dr Pranjal Modi, vice-chancellor of Gujarat University of Transplantation Sciences (GUTS) and convenor of State Organ & Tissue Transplantation Organization (SOTTO), said that the drop in Covid-19 cases have resulted in the rise in donations. ‚ÄúAll donations are conducted with utmost care and following Covid protocols. ---||Jaipur||Coercive population control measures not effective, say experts||Jaipur: With all other health programmes taking a backseat during the pandemic, the demand for increasing the focus and strengtheing the facilities for population control is rising. On World Population Day, experts claimed that coercive population control measures are not the solution and could instead lead to a potential increase in sex selection practices. This is likely to have a negative impact on the child sex ratio, affecting central government campaigns such as the Beti Bachao Beti Padhao programme. Instead, focus must be laid on bring about an awareness and encouraging them to make an informed decision. Informed consent and dignity are two areas which are repeatedly compromised when it comes to delivery of contraceptive services. ‚ÄúBoth temporary and permanent methods of contraception should be made available and accessible to all. There is a need that through public health care system people are informed to make appropriate choices without any coercion,‚Äù says Chhaya Pachauli, director, Prayas, Centre for Health Equity. ‚ÄúThe entire family planning programme must also be realigned to shift from a population control focus to that of protecting reproductive rights and choices,‚Äù she adds. Rajasthan‚Äôs population in 2021 is estimated to be 79.28 million (7.92 crore) with its youth and adolescent population pegged at 32 per cent. ‚ÄúAccording to the fourth National Family Health Survey (2015-16), more than 35 per cent of girls in Rajasthan are married before the age of 18. The 2020 Annual Status of Education Report (ASER) survey states that in Rajasthan 12.5 per cent of girls aged 15-16-year-old drop out of school due to diverse reasons, including early marriage and childbearing. The COVID-19 pandemic has further deteriorated the situation and has highlighted the need to invest in our young to convert them into demographic bonus,‚Äù says Dr Dhirendra Kumar (Population Scientist and Dean, IIHMR University). Divya Santhanam, senior state programme manager, Population Foundation of India says, ‚ÄúIn Rajasthan, work is being done by grassroots agencies and the government to promote the importance of education for girls, family planning and dispersal of information about sexual and reproductive health. The pandemic had an impact on equal access to contraceptives and safe abortions and increased the risk of teen pregnancies but the government has shown a willingness to address these issues with its outreach programs and network of adolescent friendly health centres.‚Äù For Rajasthan‚Äôs youth population, family planning and access to contraceptives is a critical element of the primary care component, given its crucial role in delaying first births, ensuring spacing between births, lowering maternal and child mortality, and preventing unsafe abortions. Action Research and Training for Health (ARTH) in Udaipur aims at increasing and expanding reproductive choice among women by giving them options to choose which contraception they would want to use. ‚ÄúBy late April 2020, we started seeing young women ‚Äî mothers of 1 to 2 children ‚Äî with anxiety writ across their faces, seeking a quick means to avoid another pregnancy after their husbands abruptly returned from cities, jobless. They were clear that this was not the time to become pregnant, and yet there was no transport to reach health facilities and government workers were busy with Covid surveys. Several others presented with unwanted pregnancies," said Dr Sharad Iyengar, chief executive of the organisation. He added that stepped up doorstep delivery of moving supplies into barricaded villages. The increase in uptake of oral contraceptive pills, condoms and single use emergency pills - which the organisation supplied even during the pandemic - was unprecedented. ‚ÄúThe focus must be on simple options that allowed self care by young women and men to avert a personal crisis,‚Äù he added.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/jaipur/coercive-population-control-measures-not-effective-say-experts/articleshow/84305703.cms||---

The child was discharged on the fifth day of the surgery after the first dose of chemotherapy. ‚ÄúShe is recuperating well. As per PPP norms, the private partner should bring in the money required for the project and so the government can shrug off the responsibility of raising funds. But in the case of the proposed waste plant at Brahmapuram, the private partner will be able to mobilize bank loans by mortgaging the corporation‚Äôs land. As per the PPP norms, the private partner should raise the funds on its own. If mortgaging corporation‚Äôs land is required for raising funds for the project, the local body itself or the government can do it. Then, there is no need for a private partner,‚Äù Austin said. According to the corporation authorities, it is the state government which decided to lease out the land. ‚ÄúKochi corporation doesn‚Äôt have any role in implementing the waste-to-energy plant project. We haven‚Äôt supported leasing out the local body‚Äôs land to a private firm,‚Äù said corporation health standing committee chairman T K Asharaf. ---||Amritsar||New plant species discovered in Antarctica named after India||BATHINDA: Polar biologists at Central University of Punjab have discovered a new native species of moss from continental Antarctica. The species is named Bryum bharatiensis‚Äì named so as a tribute to the country and India‚Äôs Antarctic station, Bharati. Felix Bast, associate professor and head of the department of Botany, Central University, who was part of Indian Antarctic Mission 2016-17 as an expedition scientist, stumbled upon these green plants on the rocks near Bharati station at Larsemann Hills, East Antarctica. He collected the samples and brought them back to the lab in the university for further work. He performed taxonomic assessments along with his PhD student, Wahid Ul Rahman and collaborator Kriti Gupta, who is heading the Botany department at DAV College, Bathinda. Subsequent studies confirmed it to be a new species of moss discovered for the first time in the world. Besides the discovery of the new species, the study also revealed two new taxonomic records. The moss Bryoerythrophyllum recurvirostrum was recorded for the first time from Larsemann Hills and the moss, Coscinodon lawianus from Schirmacher Oasis- a place near India‚Äôs yet another Antarctic Station, Maitri. Felix used an approach combining morphology-based traditional techniques with DNA sequence-based modern tools for formalising the discovery of the species. Bast said, ‚ÄúThis is the first plant species discovery resulting from 40 years of Indian Antarctic Mission, that began in 1981. India‚Äôs first Antarctic station, Dakshin Gangotri, was established in 1984 but was abandoned and decommissioned in 1990 as the station submerged in an ice sheet. Maitri station was commissioned in 1989 while Bharati station in 2012, both are currently operational and year-round stations. There had been a number of discoveries of bacterial species in Antarctica, but the way species is defined in bacteria is very different from that in plants.‚Äù It has been estimated that the planet earth has 1 trillion species of living organisms, out of which we know merely 1.2 million till date. Discovering new species like this is important not only for characterisation of the Earth‚Äôs biodiversity, but also for economic utilisation by future generations. As naturally occurring living organisms cannot be patented in India, species discoveries like this is an analogous process, he said. The paper describing the discovery has been published in the leading international journal, Journal of Asia-Pacific Biodiversity (Elsevier). This is the sixth species discovery from the research group of Felix Bast, all gthe earlier five were new species of marine seaweeds from Indian coasts.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/amritsar/new-plant-species-discovered-in-antarctica-named-after-india/articleshow/84307455.cms||---

---||Mumbai||‚ÄòSex abuse‚Äô at work: Bombay HC tells woman to move industrial court||MUMBAI: In a complaint of sexual harassment at workplace, the Bombay high court has directed a woman to file an appeal before the industrial court in Mumbai against a March 2020 POSH committee order dismissing her allegations against an executive she used to report to in a large corporate. In March, for the first time, the state had notified industrial courts as an appellate body under the Prevention of Sexual Harassment at Workplace (Prevention, Prohibition and Redressal) Act (POSH), 2013, for those not satisfied with recommendations of the internal panel. The HC said the relevance of the notification was that the industrial court would be the appellate authority under the POSH Act. The HC bench of Justices Ujjal Bhuyan and Madhav Jamdar, in a July 8 decision, said the woman can seek remedy by filing an appeal against the internal committee (IC) report and order. Under the POSH Act, a complaint is first assessed by an in-house panel which also has a member from an NGO. The woman approached the HC last year with a grievance that since the in-house panel informed her ‚Äúno action was required‚Äù on her complaint alleging sexual harassment, thereby dismissing it, she had nowhere to turn to. Her counsel, Mihir Desai, said there was no appellate body set up or notified by the state under the POSH Act or rules and hence she was constrained to approach the HC against the company to quash the IC‚Äôs report and order. She also questioned her subsequent ‚Äúillegal termination‚Äù in June 2020. The company, represented by counsel Birendra Saraf, opposed her petition and also questioned its maintainability given the provisions of the Act. At a hearing on March 11, the state had said the POSH Act, under Section 18 and Rule 11, provides for appeals against the IC report. The HC had directed the state to give details of whether such an appellate authority was set up. On July 8, the state‚Äôs assistant government pleader Hemant Haryan informed the HC of its March 31 notification. It made the industrial court in Mumbai the appellate authority in this case. The notification was issued by the state deputy secretary (industries, energy and labour departments) under Section 2 (A) of the Industrial Employment (Standing Orders) Act, 1946, in supersession of the earlier notifications. The POSH Act‚Äôs Section 18 says any person aggrieved from recommendations made under Section 13 (2) (i) or (ii) or sections 14 and 17 or non-implementation of such recommendations may file an appeal to a tribunal within 90 days. The HC bench said ‚Äúit would be open‚Äô‚Äô to the woman seeking condonation of the delay and the tribunal then may consider the time spent in pursuing the petition before the HC as well as the prevailing pandemic. It did not pass orders on maintainability of her petition or merit and kept all such contentions open. (The victim's identity has not been revealed to protect her privacy as per Supreme court directives on cases related to sexual assault)||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/mumbai/sex-abuse-at-work-hc-tells-woman-to-move-indl-court/articleshow/84307461.cms||Swati Deshpande

---||Goa||Relic of Georgian martyr St Ketevan reaches home||PANAJI: India on Friday handed over to Georgia a relic of their 17th century queen, St Ketevan, which was discovered within the ruins of the St Augustine complex, Old Goa, in 2004. ‚ÄúBlessed to hand over the holy relics of St. Queen Ketevan to the people of Georgia. An emotional moment...‚Äù said Union external affairs minister S Jaishankar. MEA S Jaishankar hands over the relics to his Georgian counterpart David ZalkalianiThe Indian government has gifted one part of the right arm bone relic to the Georgian government, while the other part continues to be in the custody of the ASI museum in Old Goa. A replica of the relics excavated are on display at the museum. At the request of the Georgian government, the relics were sent for an exhibition in 2017, and then returned to India. Ketevan, who was canonised and is venerated as a saint in the Eastern Orthodox Church, is considered a martyr in her native land, and Georgians have been anticipating the arrival of her relics. They now reach Georgia more than four centuries after they were hidden and transported ‚Äî from Iran, where she was killed, by Augustinian friars ‚Äî to Old Goa, and placed in a sarcophagus (a stone coffin) in Old Goa. ASI‚Äôs excavations at the complex lasted over a decade. When contacted, former ASI director N Taher, who led the team that uncovered the relics at the time, said it is a homecoming of sorts for the saint. ‚ÄúFor those who believe in divinity, the saint herself wanted to be exhumed for the second time by our archaeological team (of ASI) to travel back to her homeland as a gift from the people of India,‚Äù he said. Back when the relics were unearthed, the paradox was that the team was not searching for the bone relics, but for the place where the relics were kept. ‚ÄúThen, when we found the remains, we worked in reverse order to prove the bone found was that of the mother saint of Georgia. It was like a jigsaw puzzle, and all the teams associated with it tried to piece it together from their perspective and‚Ä¶ we had the right combination to open the lock,‚Äù he told TOI.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/goa/relic-of-georgian-martyr-ketevan-reaches-home/articleshow/84305881.cms||Lisa Monteiro

The Ahmedabad district court at Mirzapur disposed of more than 20,000 cases out of 33,134 cases taken up for settlement. ---||Nagpur||‚ÄòResearch in forensic science shall help both varsity & investigations‚Äô||The Government Institute of Forensic Science (IFS) got its first doctorate of philosophy (PhD) holders in assistant professors Ashish Badiye and Neeti Kapoor. Badiye, who is head of the forensic science department, was one of the founding faculty members when the IFS started from the makeshift campus at Government Institute of Science in 2011. Kapoor joined a year later and together the husband-wife duo have authored several research works published in reputed journals like Elsevier, Taylor and Francis, Springer, SAGE, Nature, etc. Their expertise is often sought by investigating authorities to help crack complex crimes. Started in 2017, the PhDs, under the guidance of Swati Dubey Mishra, was recently awarded by Shri Vaishnav Vidyapeeth Vishwavidyalaya (SVVV), Indore, Madhya Pradesh. They are probably the first researchers in the field of forensic science from the Nagpur University. Their feat marks the beginning of research and development in this stream, which is still in the process of setting up its first forensic science research centre. The teacher-couple spoke to TOI about the importance of research and the advantage of their latest techniques derived during the PhD in related investigations. Excerpts...  Q. In what way will the university gain from your achievement? A. Neeti Kapoor: The Government Institute of Forensic Science is the first in India to be ranked in 101-150 band in the prestigious NIRF2020 ranking. Now, having a Phd would help us speed up starting the first-ever research centre in Vidarbha under Nagpur University. We would be able to apply to various funding agencies and carry out important and path-breaking research projects. Meritorious students would greatly benefit. This would ensure qualified students cracking JRF and NET in forensics don‚Äôt have to go outside Nagpur for their PhDs. Research done from Nagpur would highlight the city on the research map of the world. Ashish Badiye: We as doctoral candidates had to juggle between roles and cities to complete our PhD. This is a significant challenge for students of forensic science who may decide to switch fields if they are unable to cope with the challenges. Many students have cleared NET and JRF from our institute. They have to apply to other institutes/universities offering doctoral programmes in other cities. Some have even ended up losing their JRF since they were not able to secure a seat. I hope that our achievement marks the beginning of a new chapter wherein deserving students would be able to sustain their education from the city itself. There are renowned institutions coming up or have already set up base in Nagpur so there would be ample opportunities for collaborative research works as well. Q. What was your PhD topic all about? A. NK: My study was related to determination of hand by single-digit fingerprint. There are limited studies that deal with this wherein the researchers used only a particular pattern and a few parameters for the determination of hand. A total of 2,900 fingerprints were analysed. Twenty-eight parameters were studied in ten types of fingerprints. This study confirms the findings of the earlier studies and adds novel parameters for the determination of hand from a single fingerprint. This would be of particular help to the investigators and fingerprint examiners. Q. How does it make an investigator‚Äôs job easier? A. NK: On the crime scenes, a complete set of the ten-digit fingerprints is hardly ever encountered. Determination of hand is essential to reduce the onus of the investigator and may thereby make possible the identification of the contributor. The single finger impressions are of diverse importance. They are even used in place of signature in India in several vital documents like property, agreement to sell, validated (notarized) documents, registries, bank documents, loan documents, cheques, cash withdrawal and deposit slips, competitive examination forms, attendance sheets, among others. Assessment of hand, either right or left, is one of the most vital constraints to ascertain. In the scene of occurrence, fingerprints are not encountered in a sequence. Fingerprints usually come across in a random sequence or maybe a single fingerprint received from the scene of the crime. In such case(s), the determination hand of a print is significant to determine or scrutinise the suspect. If an examiner establishes the hand, i.e., the prints belong to the right hand or left hand, it will reduce the time of investigation by further minimising the pool of suspects. Q. And what about your study? A. AB: My PhD focused on assessment of handprint to determine the sex and height. The human handprint contains a wide assortment of measurable topographies and physiognomies (physical characteristics) like the shape of the handprint, the handprint-geometry, the dermatoglyphics (skin friction ridges) patterns, and various other features. The combination of these features proves helpful in personal identification as well as identity verification. Generally, ‚Äòhandprint‚Äô is a term used synonymously with ‚Äòpalmprint‚Äô. However, it must be noted that the ‚Äòpalmprint‚Äô comprises of the print of the inner surface of the hand between the fingers and wrist while the ‚Äòhandprint‚Äô encompasses the palmprint, the digit prints (the prints of the four fingers between the first and third phalanx), the thumbprint (the print of the thumb between first and second phalanx) and the fingerprints (the prints of four fingertips and thumb tip). Q. Will this help reduce the suspect pool? A. AB: The combination of features present on the handprints, palmprints and fingerprints are unique and permanent and serve as crucial means of identification. The dimensions and characteristics present on the hand and palm are found useful for sex determination and stature estimation. Sex determination has always been a challenging task for an investigating officer. Investigators often come across the complete or incomplete palmprints and handprints along with fingerprints at the crime scene. Various dermatoglyphic characteristics present on the palm would be helpful to determine the sex of the donor, which ultimately helps the investigator to narrow down the suspect pool to almost half. Once the sex is determined, appropriate formulae may be applied for the estimation of stature, reducing the suspect pool further. A total of 1,016 bilateral handprints were analysed.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/nagpur/research-in-forensic-science-shall-help-both-varsity-investigations/articleshow/84304009.cms||Sarfaraz Ahmed

---||Thiruvananthapuram||Strict vector control steps in Thiruvananthapuram||THIRUVANANTHAPURAM: Even though 14 of the 15 persons infected with Zika virus in the district have recovered from the symptoms, the presence of the infective vectors in the community is a major public health concern. District collector Navjot Khosa convened a high level meeting on Saturday to review the situation in the district in which district medical officer and officials in charge of surveillance and communicable diseases attended. In the meeting, the district health administration observed that the patients have recovered from the symptoms and hence they would not transmit the disease. However, the presence of the infective vectors in the community is a major public health concern. Though this is not a severe disease in the general population, it becomes a concern if it infects pregnant women in their early trimester, the meeting pointed out. The district disaster management authority has decided that focus should be given to vector management and care should be given to prevent transmission of infection to pregnant women. Measures to control mosquito breeding indoors and in peridomestic areas is the only way to contain the spread of infections in the community. The district collector has urged the health department to ensure that the district vigilance committee unit of health services department conduct vector surveillance in Thiruvananthapuram corporation area and provide technical advisories to the local self-government for mosquito control activities. In addition to this, fever clinics should be started and strengthened in all peripheral institutions. Steps shall be taken to provide awareness regarding personal protective measures against mosquito bites in antenatal clinics. The district surveillance officer and district programme manager of the national health mission should ensure that Zika containment awareness is imparted to the urban medical officers and ASHA workers. Measures should be taken to ensure strict deferral of blood donors with history of fever in the previous two weeks. All ultra sound scanning centres have been directed to report incidences of microcephally (a condition in which a baby‚Äôs head is significantly smaller than expected) during regular antenatal scans. All the local bodies in the district have been asked to start mosquito control activities in public places and uninhabited area. Municipal health services shall do fogging and spraying as per the technical directions. The ward-level health sanitation committees (WHSC) have been entrusted with the task of source reduction of mosquitoes activities. The ward level health sanitation members should take steps to inspect residential areas/public and private offices for mosquito breeding. Once in a week, all houses, including flats, should be visited and directions to eliminate the source should be given. Follow up visits after two days should be done to ensure that they have complied with instructions, the collector has said in her order.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/thiruvananthapuram/strict-vector-control-steps-in-dist/articleshow/84304031.cms||---

---||Thiruvananthapuram||Fisherman killed as boat capsizes||Thiruvananthapuram: A 40-year-old fisherman died on Saturday after his motorized boat failed and was caught in strong waves off the coast of Perumathura. John Paul of Ennakkidangu Purayidam House, Anchuthengu is the deceased. According to the police, the mishap occurred around 10.30am while Paul and fellow fishermen were returning to the shore after a nightlong fishing trip. He was part of a three-member crew that had set out into the sea from Anchughengu in a small boat fitted with an outboard engine. Paul was the one who was operating the outboard motor of the boat. The two fishermen who survived the mishap told the police that as the boat reached a distance of around three kilometres from the shore, its engine failed. However, strong winds and the current helped them drift close to the shore near Perumathura, around 500m south of the Muthalapozhi breakwater here. But, as they got closer to the shore, the intensity of the waves got stronger. They realized that the boat would crash against the shore owing to strong waves. Had it happened, the survival chances would have been lower. Hence they decided to abandon the boat and swim to the shore. While the two others managed to swim to safety, Paul could not. He drowned just a few metres away from the shore. His friends immediately dived back into the sea and helped him get to the shore. He was rushed to Chirayinkeezh Government District Hospital, but the doctors declared him dead on arrival. The police suspect that besides the strong waves, exhaustion might also have played a key role in the death of Paul. His friends told the police that until the moment they decided to abandon the boat, Paul was desperately trying to repair the motor and restart it. Paul is the fourth person to lose life in the sea at Anchuthengu. Three weeks ago, a five-year-old boy had died after he was swept away by strong waves while standing close to the sea along with his brother. Two days later, a 19-year-old man drowned after his boat capsized near Perumathura. A week later, a 57-year-old fisherman died after his boat capsized at the mouth of Muthalapozhi breakwater, which is a danger zone for the fishermen using small boats. All these mishaps, including the death of Paul on Saturday, have happened while the district collector‚Äôs warning to stay away from the sea based on weather alerts was in effect. The collector had issued a warning on Friday asking fishermen not to venture into the sea till Tuesday after India Meteorological Department predicted strong winds with speed ranging from 40 to 45 km/hour along the coasts of Kerala, Karnataka and Lakshadweep. The collector has on Saturday extended the ban till Wednesday.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/thiruvananthapuram/fisherman-killed-as-boat-capsizes/articleshow/84304087.cms||---
---||Hyderabad||Bonalu in Telangana started during the reign of the Qutb Shahi rulers in 1675||HYDERABAD: Bonalu is a traditional festival of Telangana that is celebrated annually in the month of Ashada Masam, which falls in July and continues till August. According to city-based historians, Bonalu began during the reign of Qutb Shahi rulers in 1675. Abul Hasan Tanisha‚Äôs minister Madana built a temple for Ellamma on Golconda Fort, where the first Bonam was offered to mark the month-long celebrations. The main part of the celebrations is offering bonam (meal) to appease the goddesses for protecting families from diseases. Women carry an earthen pot on their heads adorned with neem leaves, turmeric and a lamp on the top of the pot and offer them to the temple deities. The famous Lashkar Bonalu started much after Golconda Bonalu. According to historians, Suriti Ayyappa, a doli-bearer in the military, visited Mahankali temple at Ujjain in Madhya Pradesh in 1815 and was shocked to see that thousands of people died of cholera. After the decline in cholera cases and restoration of normalcy, he built a temple dedicated to Mahankali at Lashkar in Secunderabad.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/hyderabad/bonalu-in-t-started-during-the-reign-of-the-qutb-shahi-rulers-in-1675/articleshow/84306106.cms||Sunil Mungara

---||Thiruvananthapuram||Local bodies to tap own fund for VGF||Thiruvananthapuram: The local bodies in the district will have to divert money from own fund or plan fund to make up for shortage of income to Haritha Karma Sena workers during lockdown. The local self-government department (LSGD) has recently directed the local bodies to tap own/plan fund to raise viability gap fund (VGF) to make up for the income deficit of members of Haritha Karma Sena. Haritha Karma Sena workers who thrive on user fee collected from households and commercial establishments/shops have been unable to meet their needs due to practical difficulties in waste collection owing to the spread of Covid-19. The city corporation officials said that at present, civic body may not need to divert money from own fund to provide VGF for Haritha Karma Sena. The shops have remained closed due to restrictions and health concerns had prevented the workers from engaging in waste collection at houses where Covid-positive persons were quarantined. This has deprived the workers of basic income on March, April and May. Suchitwa Mission executive director reported that Haritha Karma Sena workers have been active on the field despite the challenges and that it was imperative to ensure basic income for them. The director suggested utilizing VGF for the purpose. LSGD has given sanction to the proposal. Local self-government secretaries will ensure that on the days when the workers are on duty, they will receive a basic daily wage of Rs 750. VGF shall be used to bridge the gap between expected monthly income and actual income. As per the document prepared for the functioning of Haritha Karma Sena workers, income from user fee, amount collected from sale of scrap and other items are the sources of monthly income. The department has directed that special wages shall be disbursed for the workers if local bodies engage them in services other than door-to-door collection and segregation of non-biodegradable materials. The department has however pointed out that VGF shall not be given in local bodies where basic duties were not fulfilled in spite of ideal circumstances. All local bodies which have not made Haritha Karma Sena functional have been directed to make it operational within three months. In 2018, the government had permitted local bodies to utilize specified amount from plan fund to provide VGF for six months for the activities of Haritha Karma Sena. The amount was approved at rates of Rs 23,175 per ward in gram panchayat, Rs 46,350 per ward in municipalities and Rs 92,700 per ward in corporation.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/thiruvananthapuram/local-bodies-to-tap-own-fund-for-vgf/articleshow/84304122.cms||---

---||Mumbai||Mumbai: From results in under a minute to minimal infra, testing tech evolves||MUMBAI: New Covid-19 tests, including one that promises a diagnosis within a minute, will be launched next week, pointing to a sea change in detection technologies over the past 15 months in the country. While multinational Abbott will launch a new rapid test, Mumbai-based company, MediCircle Health Pvt Ltd, will bring Israeli technology to detect the Covid-19-causing SARS-CoV-2 virus in saliva swab or gargled water within seconds. The Indian Council of Medical Research (ICMR) and National Institute of Virology (NIV) have also transferred their new technology‚Äîcalled RT-LAMP‚Äîthat allows an RT-PCR test to be done within three hours as opposed to the regular four to six hours. Dr Nilesh Shah, chief of science and innovation, Metropolis Laboratory, said Covid-19 diagnostics have changed immensely in the past 15 to 16 months. ‚ÄúThe RT-PCR test remains the gold standard, but it too has evolved in terms of requirement of time, manpower and incubation period,‚Äù he said. The new RT-PCR tests can deliver results in a matter of five minutes, though they carry premium charges of up to Rs 4,500. However, with some countries such as the UAE demanding RT-PCR reports that are taken four hours before boarding, such quick RT-PCR have takers. RT-PCR tests, though, due to their huge infrastructure and investment requirements cannot be used for mass testing easily. This is where rapid ‚Äúpoint of care‚Äù tests that can deliver results in under 15 minutes are useful. Pranav Kolhi of MediCircle Health said their new test not only gives results in less than a minute, these are transferred to the ICMR‚Äôs Covid portal instantly. ‚ÄúThere is no question of a positive test, done using a rapid antigen method or a home-based test, not getting registered,‚Äù he added. This will help trace cases and carry out public health measures to check any spread. A pilot study done in Delhi among 207 samples showed that the test has 93.5% sensitivity. ‚ÄúAs it is a point of care technology, it can be used for mass screening at airport, resorts, offices, malls, etc,‚Äù added Kohli. The Israeli test works on the principle that when infected by the virus, the body produces chemicals that emit a certain wavelength. ‚ÄúWhen a sample from the patient is inserted into our hand-held device, a spectra is generated, giving instant analysis,‚Äù said the press release. Dr Shah of Metropolis said that in the earlier days of Covid, the rapid antigen tests were not very accurate, but the tests available now are very sensitive. ‚ÄúWe have tests that use breath, voice, smell, and gargle to detect Covid,‚Äù said Dr Shah. Consider a football match where an audience needs to be tested in the shortest possible time before being let into the stadium. ‚ÄúA rapid test such as smell would require people to breathe out on a special sheet of paper and answer a few questions on their mobile. All these steps take a minute before the result is available. If you get a barcode, you can enter the stadium. If not, you need to proceed for the RT-PCR test for a confirmation test,‚Äù said Dr Shah. An ICMR press release said, ‚ÄúThe World Health Organization has urgently demanded an extension of screening and testing. With this, to address the Covid-19 pandemic, an accurate, low-cost and user-friendly diagnostic method is the need of the hour, and so, RT-LAMP is ideal for the nation‚Äôs requirements and conditions.‚Äù ICMR officials said there is an urgent need to build the testing capacity of India. ‚ÄúThe RT-LAMP method‚Äôs speed and simplicity allow it to be the ideal method for diagnosing the infection,‚Äù they added.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/mumbai/mumbai-from-results-in-under-a-minute-to-minimal-infra-testing-tech-evolves/articleshow/84306184.cms||---

The drug was meant to be smuggled to Maldives. Fernandez was acting as a middleman between the buyer identified as Abdullah, a Maldivian citizen, and the seller, who was identified as Ullas of Idukki.
