---||Business||Amul wins its first trademark violation case outside India||VADODARA: Canada has recognised ‚ÄòThe Taste of India‚Äô. The Intellectual Property Appellate Board of Canada recently accorded trademark status to India‚Äôs homegrown dairy giant Amul. The country‚Äôs largest co-operative will also be awarded damages to the tune of Canadian dollar (CAD) 32,733 after it won a trademark violation case filed in the Federal Court of Canada. It is the first such case that Amul had filed against any company on foreign soil. The Kaira District Cooperative Milk Producers Union Limited (popularly known as Amul Dairy) and the Gujarat Co-operative Milk Marketing Federation (GCMMF) that markets brand Amul had moved the Federal Court of Canada against Amul Canada and four others ‚Äî Mohit Rana, Akash Ghosh, Chandu Das and Patel (The first name not know). In January 2020, Amul learnt that the group had blatantly copied the trademark ‚ÄòAmul‚Äô and the logo of ‚ÄòAmul-The Taste of India‚Äô and created a fake profile on social media platform LinkedIn. Amul Canada also had an icon to ‚Äúsee jobs‚Äù and ‚Äúfollow‚Äù on its LinkedIn page while the four defendants were listed as employees of Amul Canada. Despite several attempts of service of the suit on the defendants, the defendants never responded. Amul‚Äôs counsels later brought an ex-parte motion for default judgement. They argued that Amul had never licensed nor provided consent for either Amul Canada or any of the four individuals to use their trademarks and copyrights in any manner. The Federal Court of Canada held that Amul has clearly satisfied all the elements for establishing ‚Äúpassing off‚Äù test being ‚Äî existence of goodwill, deception of public due to misrepresentation, actual or potential damages to Amul. The Federal Court held that the defendants had infringed the copyright of Amul and issued order permanently restraining them from infringing the trademark and copyright of ‚ÄòAmul‚Äô and ‚ÄòAmul-The Taste of India‚Äô. GCMMF has been exporting milk products to USA for the last 22 years. It has started exporting Amul Kool (flavoured milk), ice cream and dairy snacks to Canada over the last two years. Amul is globally eighth largest milk processor handling 10.3 million metric tonnes of milk annually with a turnover of over Rs 40,000 crore (CAD 9 billion). The dairy giant‚Äôs counsel in India for the case was Suhrita Majumdar, intellectual property lawyer from S Majumdar & Co., New Delhi. In Canada, it was represented by Michael Adams, intellectual property lawyer from Riches McKenzie & Herbert LLP.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//business/india-business/amul-wins-its-first-trademark-violation-case-outside-india/articleshow/84310708.cms||Prashant Rupera

Otherwise, they would have to struggle a lot to make the registration and vaccination possible,‚Äù said R K Rahul, the convenor of the library. Aiming at complete immunisation, these youngsters formed the Aksharasena Covid vaccination help desk and through a WhatsApp group, collected the details of residents needing help. During the initial phase, they collected information on the people eligible for vaccination in their families. After completing their registrations successfully, they extended their activities to other residents too. Besides the locals of Pulichamala, people residing in different areas of Palode and Vithura also benefited from their service. They also ensured that people received their jabs at the scheduled time. ‚ÄúIf they found it difficult to visit the vaccination centre, we also made necessary arrangements,‚Äù said Rahul. The help desk which functions at the library has nearly 22 volunteers. When the stringent lockdown restrictions were lifted, the volunteers visited houses to collect the details of people who were not yet registered for vaccination. Also, these youngsters provided an awareness regarding the need to get vaccinated. ‚ÄúSome were hesitant to be vaccinated. They were confused about the need to get the vaccination. In such cases, we gave them awareness regarding the same and convinced them to get vaccinated,‚Äù said Rahul. The maximum registration they did on a day was 32. The team is not done yet. They are now helping the relatives of the local residents who are residing in different localities.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/thiruvananthapuram/volunteers-help-people-with-vaccine-registration/articleshow/84304204.cms||---

The office of the deputy director of health, Nashik division, sends the vaccine van to the state office in Pune to collect the vaccines. The absence of straws and spoons could be because of the ban on plastics,‚Äù he said. Based on the waste collected, NCCR scientists calculated the Clean Coast Index (CCI), which was proposed by an Israeli scientist, and they rated Kovalam beach as ‚Äòdirty‚Äô. The CCI has four categories ‚Äî very dirty, dirty, clean and very clean. ---||Jaipur||As 2nd Covid wave ebbs, Rajasthan scraps weekend curfew from today||JAIPUR: With the second Covid wave ebbing steadily, the state government on Saturday decided to end the weekend curfews from Sunday as part of a slew of unlock measures. However, night curfew across the state from 11pm to 5am will continue. The fresh guidelines allow people, who have received the first dose of Covid vaccine, to go to cinema halls, multiplexes and attend exhibitions, though these places will operate with 50 per cent capacity under a specific time period. The order stated that shops and commercial institutions where 60 per cent of the staff have received the first dose of vaccine can remain open for an additional four hours from 4pm to 8pm. Similarly, restaurants have been allowed to open till 10pm, subject to certain conditions, which include Covid-appropriate behavior, proper sanitisation, regular thermal screening and use of masks. Chief minister Ashok Gehlot said though Rajasthan had recorded a decline in cases, he warned that the state as a whole was not cleared of the virus yet. ‚ÄúPeople should wear masks and take precautions to avert the third wave of the pandemic,‚Äù he said. The state government said if infection rate continued to fall in the days ahead, more relaxations and easing up of restrictions in markets and at commercial establishments might be allowed, albeit with strict compliance of Covid-appropriate behavior.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/jaipur/as-2nd-wave-ebbs-raj-scraps-weekend-curfew-from-today/articleshow/84306302.cms||---

The fresh guidelines allow people, who have received the first dose of Covid vaccine, to go to cinema halls, multiplexes and attend exhibitions, though these places will operate with 50 per cent capacity under a specific time period. The order stated that shops and commercial institutions where 60 per cent of the staff have received the first dose of vaccine can remain open for an additional four hours from 4pm to 8pm. Similarly, restaurants have been allowed to open till 10pm, subject to certain conditions, which include Covid-appropriate behavior, proper sanitisation, regular thermal screening and use of masks. Chief minister Ashok Gehlot said though Rajasthan had recorded a decline in cases, he warned that the state as a whole was not cleared of the virus yet. ‚ÄúPeople should wear masks and take precautions to avert the third wave of the pandemic,‚Äù he said. The state government said if infection rate continued to fall in the days ahead, more relaxations and easing up of restrictions in markets and at commercial establishments might be allowed, albeit with strict compliance of Covid-appropriate behavior.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/udaipur/as-2nd-wave-ebbs-raj-scraps-weekend-curfew-from-today/articleshow/84312960.cms||---
---||Mumbai||Bombay HC: Woman can appeal POSH panel‚Äôs dismissal of complaint||Mumbai: A woman approached Bombay high court last year with a grievance that since the in-house panel in the company where she worked informed her ‚Äúno action was required‚Äù on her complaint alleging sexual harassment, thereby dismissing it, she had nowhere to turn to. An HC bench of Justices Ujjal Bhuyan and Madhav Jamdar, in a July 8 decision, said the woman could file an appeal against the company‚Äôs internal committee (IC) report and order. Under the POSH Act, a complaint is first assessed by an in-house panel which also has a member from an NGO. Her counsel, Mihir Desai, said there was no appellate body set up or notified by the state under the POSH Act or rules and hence she was constrained to approach the HC against the company to quash the IC‚Äôs report and order. She also questioned her subsequent ‚Äúillegal termination‚Äù in June 2020.The company, represented by counsel Birendra Saraf, opposed her petition and also questioned its maintainability given the provisions of the Act.At a hearing on March 11, the state had said the POSH Act, under Section 18 and Rule 11, provides for appeals against the IC report. The HC had directed the state to give details of whether such an appellate authority was set up. On July 8, the state‚Äôs assistant government pleader, Hemant Haryan, informed the HC of its March 31 notification. It made the industrial court in Mumbai the appellate authority in this case, he said.The notification was issued by the state deputy secretary (industries, energy and labour departments) under Section 2 (A) of the Industrial Employment (Standing Orders) Act, 1946. The POSH Act‚Äôs Section 18 says any person aggrieved by the report may file an appeal to a tribunal within 90 days.The HC bench did not pass orders on maintainability of her petition or merit and kept all such contentions open.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/mumbai/bombay-hc-woman-can-appeal-posh-panels-dismissal-of-complaint/articleshow/84306296.cms||---

The story dates to a 1990 concert when a 22-year-old Sanjay broke into an impromptu musical piece that convinced senior critic N M Narayanan ‚Äî known for leaving concerts just before the ‚Äòtani avartanams‚Äô ‚Äî to walk back to his seat and stay for the rest of the show. The musician, along with Bhargavii Mani of Edge Design House started creating short episodes for digital audiences at the beginning of last year after the pandemic. Today, it has become a ritual his fans look forward to every week, in a way to get to know him better, begin candid conversations and perhaps become friends. Soon after the pandemic began, concerts were recorded and uploaded online to give audiences their fill in the absence of physical shows. And artists have broken the walls further this year with short, innovative content and talks that take them closer to their fans in a way a coffee table conversation would, albeit virtually. And with newer apps like Clubhouse streamlining these possibilities, they sure are having a lot of fun. "The stories I have been sharing here have been a staple for me at most after-dinner conversations. Close friends and family are familiar with them. I have been able to connect to newer audiences and the feedback has been fantastic," says Sanjay, who has started another series, ‚ÄòShort Notes‚Äô, on similar lines. In recent months, senior dancer Anita Ratnam started using her Instagram handle to talk about everything that constitutes her life beyond dance. She‚Äôs done close to 50 sessions in two-and-a-half months ‚Äî on everything from yoga and nutrition to fashion and leisure. She‚Äôs also taken to Clubhouse every Monday to bring together artist friends from across the globe to talk about their work and life through the pandemic. She says that offering these glimpses into her life has led to "amplifying my interests and engaging with people who interest me." "I‚Äôm doing things I would have never normally thought about, and finding in the process that there is so much more to life," says Anita. "I have a diverse following ‚Äî friends from the corporate world, journalism and the allied arts. I am pleasantly surprised to discover that I enjoy these conversations. I feel engaged and not depressed or yearning to go back on stage. That will happen when it happens." Sudha Raghunathan too has been hosting Clubhouse rooms on various music-related topics for more than a month. She says the sessions have brought her closer to people she may never have known through shows. "I meet artists, writers and journalists and interact with them on various issues, all real-time. It bridges the gap, opens us up to different opinions and leads to vibrant exchange of ideas. There‚Äôs so much creativity that can come out of this."||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/chennai/musicians-strike-the-right-note-online/articleshow/84304299.cms||Saranya Chakrapani

---||Chennai||Tamil Nadu: 1 lakh seats in 143 govt colleges to be filled online||CHENNAI: In view of the ongoing pandemic, the directorate of collegiate education (DCE) is planning to conduct online admissions to fill more than one lakh seats in 143 government arts and science colleges like last year. The directorate has gathered details such as allotted strength, admitted strength, popular courses and courses with fewer admissions from all colleges to prepare for online admissions. As per the announcement by higher education minister K Ponmudi, admission to undergraduate courses will begin from August 1 after the declaration of CBSE and state board Class XII results. ‚ÄúThe DCE is updating the website with details like new colleges and courses for 2021-22. Online applications will be user-friendly and students can fill in the details using their mobile phones,‚Äù sources said. Like last year, there will be a facilitation centre in each district to help the students. Last year, around three lakh applications were received for 89,000 seats in government colleges. The government will conduct counselling for 41 university constituent colleges that have been converted into government colleges. So, there will be around 17,000 additional seats available this year. Students are likely to be allowed to apply to any number of colleges and courses. But, they have to pay a processing fee for each college. The admissions committee will send the details of applications to each course to the concerned college. The college admissions committee will prepare the rank list based on 69% reservation. Students will be intimated about the selection list and they will be admitted after verification of certificates. ‚ÄúStudents need to be allowed to choose a medium of instruction and shift to simplify the admission process. The state government also should think of conducting admissions at regional level to make the online admission process more efficient,‚Äù said T Veeramani, president of TN Government Collegiate Teachers‚Äô Association . Last year, colleges prepared rank lists for BA, BSc and BCom based on the marks scored on four subjects excluding languages. The rank list for BA Tamil was prepared based on Class XII Tamil marks and BA English literature was English marks.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/chennai/1-lakh-seats-in-143-govt-colleges-to-be-filled-online/articleshow/84304406.cms||---

---||Chennai||Meet the wordly wise||CHENNAI: For Japanese language learners in Tamil Nadu, employment is the driving force behind their desire for fluency. For the Korean language learners, it‚Äôs entertainment ‚Äî K-pop, K-cosmetics, K-food, K-cool are hotter than ever now. Meanwhile, those waitlisted for emigration to Canada are using the time indoors to fast-track their French. Whatever the reasons, language learning has seen a spike in the past year-and-a-half of the lockdown. In its 2020 report, language learning app Duolingo said more than 30 million people started learning a language on the app in the weeks following the outbreak of the pandemic (March-April), which was 70% more than during the same period in 2019. Software engineer Shankara Narayanan from Salem was one of those new learners. His language of choice ‚Äî Japanese. "I completed one part of the course last year and its corresponding exam in December," says the 22-year-old who has wasted no time since then in his job search. "Employers in Japan are more responsive because I know the basics of the language. In terms of a salary, I know I can earn at least 80% more than in India," says Narayanan. Anuradha Rajasekaran, director at ABK-AOTS DOSOKAI, the oldest Japanese language school in south India, says in the four decades since its establishment, the largest number of enrolments has been in the past year. "The external affairs ministry reached out to Japanese schools across the country recently and highlighted the fact that 3.5 lakh people are required in Japan for jobs ranging from nursing to farming as the country has an aging population," says Rajasekaran. "Our biggest surprise was the interest we are seeing from the semi-urban areas, the reason being that with the classes online, more people have the opportunity to learn." At the INKO Centre, where Korean is taught, director Rathi Jaffer says they have a waiting list of 300 for the online language classes. "While a few years ago, learning Korean was linked to employability on account of the plethora of Korean companies in the city, nowadays it‚Äôs to do with the popularity of K-pop, K-fashion, K-food, K-drama and so on," says Jaffer. From rural Tamil Nadu, several states in the northeast and Kashmir, it‚Äôs a K-plosion of interest. For the past decade, ever since she got hooked to K-dramas, Shangavi Sundar has been yearning to learn Korean. "I never had the chance because the classes were in Chennai," says the 26-year-old civil engineer from Cuddalore. But within a couple of months of the Covid-19 lockdown, she signed up with Inko for online classes in the language. "It‚Äôs been a year. I‚Äôm thinking of switching careers and becoming an interpreter," she says. Sprachlingua, another language school in the city, which focuses on the more practical aspects of language learning such as business communication, says French and Spanish have seen an uptake during the lockdown. German and Chinese seeing the least number of takers, although the numbers here are also slowly climbing, says Sreeram Mahaalingam, co-founder of the school. ‚ÄúWith executives not being able to travel, client management takes place over emails and phone calls. That‚Äôs the reason we have a number of working professionals reaching out to learn languages,‚Äù adds Sudha Suresh, another co-founder. She says that several emigrants to Canada had enrolled for French classes while waiting for their visas to come through. As for intrepid Japanese language learner Narayanan, with a job on the horizon, he says he has moved on to researching Japanese culture and cuisine. "I now need to know vegetarian food options in Japan."||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/chennai/meet-the-wordly-wise/articleshow/84304481.cms||Kamini Mathai

On Saturday, Mother Dairy said that procurement cost of milk from dairy farmers has gone up by 8-10% in the last one year. Other operational costs have also risen, necessitating the retail hike. However, the head of Maharashtra's dairy major Gokul milk cooperative Satej Patil, who is also minister of state for home, attributed the price rise to a hike in procurement costs. The launch of these stations complements Amazon India‚Äôs efforts to increase opportunities for women in the logistics sector whilst strengthening its diversity, equity and inclusivity (DEI) commitment. The company already has two all-women delivery stations in Chennai and Kadi, Gujarat. The DSP programme is a last-mile delivery model where Amazon India partners with small and mid-sized businesses (SMBs) to deliver packages to Amazon customers. For many partners, this programme is their first entrepreneurial venture. They leverage their local knowledge of the community and the technological support offered by Amazon India to seamlessly fulfil delivery promises to customers. The launch of the stations in these towns not only enables Amazon India to deepen its reach to customers in and around these areas but also provide growth and work opportunities for DSPs and the associates they hire. These stations are completely managed and run by women across managerial and delivery associate roles. All associates are provided with training support across different aspects, including customer service, handling packages, technology and safety, said a press statement from Amazon India. The company has introduced several measures to ensure a safe workplace for women by creating awareness and building various feedback mechanisms, and a dedicated helpline number created for associates to dial in for any support or help needed during the day. Speaking about the launch of these stations, Prakash Rochlani, director, Last Mile Operations, Amazon India, said, ‚ÄúThe launch of these two all-woman delivery stations in Kerala is an extension of our continuous efforts to provide women with safe and fulfilling opportunities and we remain steadfast in our resolve to financially uplift them.‚Äù Amazon India has said in its media statement that it is committed towards building a diverse, equitable and inclusive workforce and is empowering individuals from various communities.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/kochi/amazon-launches-two-all-woman-delivery-stns/articleshow/84302797.cms||---

---||Delhi||With 61% deficit, parched Delhi yearns for monsoon||NEW DELHI: The capital is crying for rain having recorded a precipitation deficit of 61% from the normal since June 1. The India Meteorological Department has accordingly placed Delhi in the ‚Äòlarge deficient‚Äô area category. While five of nine districts are in a deficient rainfall category, four suffered a large deficiency. The city has so far received only 44.1mm of rain since June 1 against the normal mark of 114.2mm. IMD data shows that North district has so far fared the best in terms of precipitation, receiving 78mm of rainfall between June 1 and July 10. However, the normal mark for the district until July 10 is 103.3mm, therefore, placing it at a deficit of 25%. The Central district has fared the worst, receiving just 8.5mm of rainfall during this period compared with the normal of 118.9mm, indicating a deficit of 93%. IMD classifies rainfall as ‚Äòdeficit‚Äô when the precipitation is 19% or more below the normal and ‚Äòlarge deficit‚Äô or ‚Äòlarge deficient‚Äô when this figure is more than -59%. Between -19% and 19% of the normal, the rainfall is classified as ‚Äònormal‚Äô and between 20% and 59% as ‚Äòexcess‚Äô. The other districts in the large deficient category are North-East (-65%), South (-79%) and South-West (-70%), these having barely received any rain, even during the recent wet spells. Met officials, however, explained that anomalies in the distribution of rainfall, especially before the arrival of the monsoon rains, was common and the distribution of rainfall stabilised once the monsoon showers hit the city. ‚ÄúWhen the rainy season starts, the spread will be more even and the deficits will likely be bridged. Good rainfall is expected this week, and this should lead to the reduction of the overall deficit. A delay of around two weeks in the monsoons reaching Delhi caused this deficit to build up,‚Äù said an official. Last year, Delhi had a head start on June 25 with the monsoon hitting the capital two days before the scheduled arrival. IMD officials said that though the monsoon may arrive early, Delhi starts receiving spells of moderate to heavy rainfall consistently only towards the end of July and in August. ‚ÄúDelhi has a small area, so some parts may not receive rainfall at all during certain spells. Significant changes will be seen once heavy rainfall occurs, which generally happens towards the end of July and in August,‚Äù said the official. Watch Delhi cries for rain, records precipitation deficit of 61%||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/delhi/with-61-deficit-parched-capital-yearns-for-monsoon/articleshow/84304583.cms||Jasjeev Gandhiok

The bench passed the judgment accepting the reference of the trial court to confirm the capital sentence already awarded to the man in 2016 and dismissing his appeal. While issuing notice, the top court said it was surprised no one had challenged the Act all these years. People like Salman‚Äôs father, Hakeem Khan, a businessman, feel that PD Act should be used only against those who are involved in murder, attempt to rape, dacoity and other serious offences as the accused pose threat to society. It should not be invoked against accused facing charges like cheating and white-collar offences. ‚ÄúExcept in the case filed against my son at the Chandrayangutta police station, the other four cases were filed without any evidence,‚Äù Khan claimed. ‚ÄúIt has become common practice for police to file multiple cases just to create grounds for invoking the PD Act.‚Äù Take the case of an astrologer in Nalgonda district who obtained bail in four cheating cases after being in jail. However, for the past three months, he is still in jail as the PD Act has been slapped on him. Using the PD Act against an accused who has already obtained bail, is violation of his right to freedom and right to obtain bail. Police have been invoking the PD Act based on assumptions and presumptions. Instead of using the Act, the police should seek cancellation of bail if the accused repeats an offence in violation of bail conditions.‚Äù A senior Telangana police officer told TOI, ‚ÄúThe Supreme Court has not taken an objection to the law. The judges have sought an affidavit, which is a legal procedure. With regard to the observation that it is a draconian law, it is for Parliament, assembly and the Supreme Court to decide whether it should be changed or scrapped. The Andheri-based woman, Harsha Lala, was being taken to the OPD from the gate in a wheelchair handled by the hospital security guard when she fell on the ramp. The national commission observed that most wheelchair injuries happen in a medical setting due to the negligence of medical staff, and they could easily be prevented by the hospital or nursing home. ‚ÄúAs a word of caution, in my view, the hospital authority should make systemic improvement in their administration and their grievance redressal mechanism to ensure the patient‚Äôs safety and to maintain good doctor-relationship,‚Äù presiding member Dr S M Kantikar said. No jurisdictional error, or legal principle ignored, or miscarriage of justice, is visible,‚Äù the state commission said. Lala arrived at the hospital on October 9, 2012 for a follow-up check-up. She had undergone a spinal surgery in the last week of September 2012. As a result, Lala suffered a ‚Äòhead-on fall‚Äô from the wheelchair and sustained a fracture in the left ankle. She further alleged that immediate first aid was not given and she was made to stand in queue for payment of X-ray charges, which caused further pain and agony. In May, cybersecurity firm ESET issued a specific warning for India saying fake messages, linked to Covid1-9 vaccination, were sneaking malware into mobile phones. "Android SMS worm tries to spread via text messages as fake free registration for Covid-19 vaccine - targets India. It can spread itself via SMS to victim contacts with link to download this malware," said ESET researcher Lukas Stefanko in a tweet. Citizens have been submitting such messages to the Times Verified service for checks. Since its launch on April 30, Times Verified has helped bust nearly 800 fake messages linked to the pandemic ‚Äî everything from vaccine-triggered "human magnetism" to the existence of a global cabal that's attempting "population control" through the jabs. Scientists from around the world have said that such messages should not be trusted. The experts have also asked citizens to rely on reliable news outlets and scientific organisations to avoid falling prey to fake claims, which can derail public health measures. One study found that the single largest category of misleading or false claims (39%) are "mischaracterizations or misleading messages about actions or policies of public authorities".||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/pune/beware-of-fake-texts-posts-linked-to-vaccine-drives/articleshow/84304765.cms||---

---||Madurai||Terracotta container unearthed in Keeladi||Madurai: A terracotta container unearthed at the archaeological site at Keeladi in Sivaganga during the seventh phase of excavation, has an intricately designed band running along its outer surface. It is not known if this is a part of a ring well or grain storing unit, as it has many layers.Archaeology minister Thangam Thennarasu mentioned on social media that another interesting artefact, a container with designs was the latest find, and added that Keeladi continues to be a treasure trove that intrigues many.This container is 77cm in diameter, and has a two centimeter thick rim. The decorations on the container have attracted the attention of archaeologists. It has depressions such as thumb impressions and another has a band which has been equally divided into small squares, with deep lines in between. Both the decorations are two centimetres thick Deputy director of archaeology and site director R Sivanantham said they found the container a day ago, and when they continued to dig further they found another similar ring. He said only further digging would confirm if the structure was a part of a ring well, many of which have already been found in Keeladi for storing water or grains. Sources say it is inspiring to find out that those of a bygone era approached everything, including basic needs with creativity. The ring wells unearthed in Keeladi, have an interlocking system where sand cannot enter the wells, but air and water could percolate through them. It is believed that these structures helped the inhabitants of Keeladi to have more permanent dwellings and as they had water and did not have the need to migrate during droughts. They are not mere structures. They are pieces of art, they said.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/madurai/terracotta-container-unearthed-in-keeladi/articleshow/84304736.cms||---

---||Mumbai||Maha contingent hailed by Hitler & given a medal during Olympics||Dhyan Chand, the hockey legend who had reportedly played without shoes during the second half of India‚Äôs historic final against Germany at the 1936 Berlin Olympics wasn‚Äôt the only barefooted athlete to bring home a gold medal that year. An army of pheta-sporting Maharashtrian and Gujarati men, who had marched behind the British-flag-carrying official Indian Olympic contingent with a curious saffron flag bearing symbols like the tricolour, an upward arrow and a star, returned from the Games with two special gold medals, one of which is known locally as the ‚ÄòHitler Medal‚Äô. By balancing themselves atop a malkhamb pole, squatting for rounds of kho-kho, chanting ‚Äòhu tu tu‚Äô in kabaddi and contorting into yoga asanas, 24 sportsmen from Amravati‚Äôs Hanuman Vyayam Prasarak Mandal, set up in 1914, won an Olympic medal with the Nazi symbol of an eagle clutching a swastika. It was their prize for standing second in ‚Äúphysical culture display‚Äù at the World Pedagogic Congress, where nations showcased their indigenous sports. How desi team got ‚ÄòVande Mataram‚Äô played at a Berlin Olympic banquetAmong the Mumbaikars in the Indian contingent that ended up winning a medal at the first-of-its-kind International Sports Pedagogic Congress during the Berlin Olympics in 1936 were Vile Parle‚Äôs Nagindas Mehta and Premji Rajoda, G G Rajderkar, S V Kher and a strapping, 21-year-old sports teacher from Parel named Dattaram Lad aka ‚ÄòLad Master‚Äô. The idea of the first-of-its-kind congress, where various nations showcased their indigenous sports, was born from a friendship between Amravati‚Äôs Hanuman Vyayam Prasarak Mandal stalwart L J Kokardekar, who had been studying in Berlin in the 1930s, and Carl Diem, chief organiser of the 1936 Olympic Games, said mandal director Suresh Deshpande. In a letter to Kokardekar, S D Sondhi, secretary of the fledgling Indian Olympic Association, wrote: ‚ÄúI am taking steps to send your gymnasts‚Äô names (sic) for the Sports Pedagogic Congress where only, according to Diem, your gymnasts can give displays.‚Äù This largely crowdfunded trip to Berlin saw the athletes sailing in an Italian ship called 'Kamteverde' to Venice, bonding with Chinese sportsmen and taking a train to Germany. According to a TOI article, the opening ceremony of the Games saw the earthy team singing Rabindranath Tagore‚Äôs ‚ÄòEkla Chalo Re‚Äô. A barley-based health drink called Biomalt was favoured by Austria, which stood first in physical culture display, while ‚Äúcurry, meats including mutton, veal, lamb and fowl but no beef, pork or beef suet‚Äù formed the special dietary requests of India‚Äôs contingents that year, as per a sports portal. When photos of the desi flexers led by Yavatmal physician Dr S K Kane dotted German newspapers the day after their demonstrations, an intrigued Adolf Hitler invited the pehelwans for an interaction, recalls Kane‚Äôs 89-year-old son Padmakar. The Nazi leader had presented his father with a special medal, a certificate with his signature and a question that Kane would repeat on cue for the rest of his life. ‚ÄúDoes your team represent the average Indian?‚Äù Hitler had apparently asked Kane, referring to the brigade whose spines had been proclaimed by an official as ‚Äúthe most perfect‚Äù after examination. When every participating nation‚Äôs national anthem was played during an event in Berlin, the official Indian team stood up for the British national anthem ‚ÄòGod save the queen‚Äô but the desi army didn‚Äôt, says Kane‚Äôs son Padmakar. ‚ÄúMy father was a nationalist by temperament. He told his team to remain seated through it,‚Äù recalls Padmakar, adding that when a German minister probed them, the musclemen said that they considered ‚ÄòVande Mataram‚Äô to be their national anthem. ‚ÄúThe minister asked them for a recording. That‚Äôs how ‚ÄòVande Mataram‚Äô came to be played at the official banquet,‚Äù says Padmakar, adding that his father had come in contact with Bengal‚Äôs Yugantar, a secret revolutionary party that had started under the guise of a fitness club, while studying medicine in Bengal. HVPM‚Äôs website makes no secret of the mandal‚Äôs own nationalism-doused mythology. Founded by the Vaidya brothers, Anant and Ambadas, who wanted to link physical education with the Independence movement, the mandal boasted many freedom fighters, including Shivaram Raj-guru who studied here in 1926-27. Mahatma Gandhi and Sub-has Chandra Bose visited the mandal twice. In fact, Dr S G Patwardhan, the mandal‚Äôs then president, ‚Äúcould not go to Berlin in 1936 as he was denied a passport for political reasons‚Äù, says Deshpande. Lad‚Äôs Pune-based grandson Somdutt said: ‚ÄúAfter marriage, he would often leave home at night saying he had some work. My grandmother found out he was a freedom fighter when Veer Savarkar visited him one day in the 1940s‚Ä¶ He was killed before Independence in January 1947.‚Äù His grandmother Snehlata, an archer and sports teacher, was severely scarred by the loss. ‚ÄúWhen my father, a black belt in judo, got an offer to train in Japan, she didn‚Äôt allow him to go,‚Äù says Somdutt. ‚ÄúShe didn‚Äôt want to lose any more people.‚Äù Today, only time-worn pictures and stories remain of the contingent and the mandal has taken to calling the Olympic gold medal, which sits safe in its Amravati office, the ‚ÄòHitler medal‚Äô.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/mumbai/how-desi-team-got-vande-mataram-played-at-a-berlin-olympic-banquet/articleshow/84306795.cms||Sharmila Ganesan Ram

They said the images of a conch, chakram, umbrella, stick, water jug, sun, moon, parsu and plough were carved on the rocks. The team comprising S Arulanadam Krishnakumar, S Kumaran and T Siva Raj had subsequently approached Trichy-based archaeo-symbolist T L Subash Chandira Bose to study the rock carvings.Bose says, ‚ÄúIt is a very rare and interesting finding of symbolic representation of Lord Vishnu and his three incarnations. Lord Vishnu, who is known as ‚ÄúSangu Chakra Dhaari‚Äù, is symbolically depicted as ‚Äúsangu‚Äù (conch) and ‚Äúchakram‚Äù. Umbrella, stick with a rope and water jug denote Lord Vamanar, while parasu denotes Lord Parasuraman and plough denotes Lord Balaraman.‚Äù In Srimad-Bhagavatam, he says, Vishnu‚Äôs fifth incarnation Vamana is mentioned as a brahmachari, wearing a loincloth (koupeena) and sacred thread, and holding an umbrella and a stick (dhanda) in one hand and a water jug (kamandala) in the other hand. ‚ÄúIn Vishnudharmottara Purana and Rupamandana, a man carrying an axe is described as Parasuraman, the sixth incarnation of Lord Vishnu. In Hindu mythology, Balaraman, the elder brother of Lord Krishna and considered the eighth incarnation of Lord Vishnu, carries a plough.‚ÄùThe petroglyphs, Bose says, may be referring to the land donated to the Maha Vishnu temple that existed around 16th century near Anumanthapuram in Dharmapuri district.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/salem/rock-art-on-lord-vishnus-three-avatars-found-in-dharmapuri/articleshow/84303007.cms||---

---||Delhi||Delhi: 5,0000 illegal borewells sealed, 15,000 still there||NEW DELHI: The second wave of Covid-19 pandemic in Delhi has also impacted the drive to seal illegal borewells in the city.  According to the latest status report on the illegal borewell sealing exercise, more than 20,350 illegal borewells have been surveyed across Delhi so far out of which only 5,430 have been sealed. The report, prepared by Delhi Jal Board, states that fines have been imposed in all these 5,430 cases and sealing is pending in the rest of the cases. The maximum number of violators has been found in the North West district (9,067), followed by South West Delhi (6,644) and the West district (2,185). According to the status report, 44% violators were found in North West, 32.6% in South West, 10.7% in West, 3.7% in North and 3.3% in Central Delhi. Other districts reported an even smaller number of violations. The process of sealing rest of the approximate 15,000 borewells has been resumed and officials say fines going up to Rs 5 lakh have been imposed, depending on the groundwater table of the area and the amount of water that has already been extracted. A senior government official said that district administrations were busy in dealing with Covid and the drive was halted due to the second wave, which led to the delay in completing the sealing action. Officials said that in many cases, people were also found packaging and selling the extracted water. While Delhi has installed capacity of 935 MGD (million gallons per day) water supply, the estimated demand is more than 1,250 MGD. In various parts of the capital, illegal borewells are used to meet the 300 MGD demand-supply gap. A DJB official said that many people were using illegal borewells in several planned areas to avoid crossing the usage limit under the 20KLD scheme. A DJB report on identified illegal groundwater extraction points shows that around 87% of the surveyed violators are located in North West, South West and West districts. Situation in the South West district in which Dwarka and Najafgarh belts fall is particularly alarming as the average groundwater readings are around 19.2 metres below the ground. There is a very high concentration of borewells in these areas. Even according to a Central Ground Water Board report from 2019, South Delhi district was the worst affected with average reading levels around 34.2 metres below the ground. In North Delhi, water was found just 5.7 metres below the ground. A DJB official said that action was being taken as per orders of the National Green Tribunal and the drive to seal illegal borewells would continue in the coming months. The issue of fast depleting groundwater resources in Delhi has come to the spotlight because of additional burden on the subsurface aquifers in the water-stressed city.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/delhi/5k-illegal-borewells-sealed-15k-still-there/articleshow/84305097.cms||---

---||Delhi||Be alert, but don‚Äôt panic if platelets low after Covid||NEW DELHI: Low platelet count is one of the common features of viral infections. But, in most cases, the platelets reach normal levels as soon as the infection subsides. However, in the case of Covid-19, doctors have come across patients who continue to exhibit low platelet counts for weeks after recovery. In most cases, the doctors pointed out, the deficit in platelets was marginal and didn‚Äôt require medical intervention. But there have been rare cases of patients coming with extremely low platelet counts necessitating medical management. ‚ÄúWe saw three recovered patients recently with very low 10,000-20,000 platelets per microlitre of blood. One 85-year-old man had a count of 2,000 with extensive bleeding below the skin. All of them required medical management, including administration of steroids,‚Äù said Dr Atul Gogia, senior consultant, internal medicine, Sir Ganga Ram Hospital. Dr Rommel Tickoo, director, internal medicine, Max Hospital, Saket, explained, ‚ÄúNormal platelet counts range from 1,50,000 to 4,00,000 per microlitre of blood. Of the recovered Covid patients, nearly 20% have platelet counts in the range of 1,00,000 to 1,50,000, which is low but this doesn‚Äôt necessitate any intervention. We should worry only if the platelet count reduces to 50,000 or less or if there is bleeding from the gums or the nose.‚Äù Dr Naveen Dang, consultant microbiologist and founder of Dr Dang‚Äôs Lab, said he had also seen many patients who continued to have platelets in the range of 1-1.5 lakh per microlitre of blood for weeks after recovering from the coronavirus infection. ‚ÄúIt is not something to be scared of,‚Äù he assured. Platelets are one of the cellular components of the blood along with white and red blood cells. They play an important role in clotting and bleeding. According to Dr Neeraj Nischal, an assistant professor in the medicine department of AIIMS, reduced platelet count after Covid could be caused by multiple factors, for example the administration of blood thinner drugs to treat the infection. ‚ÄúIt could also be an incidental finding and may suggest some underlying illness. The role of the novel coronavirus in disrupting the immune system to induce thrombocytopenia cannot be ruled out either, but this requires further investigation,‚Äù Nischal said. Last year, scientists from China reported a case in which a 49-year-old woman showed a very low platelet count for nearly four months after recovering from non-severe Covid. They attributed it to the damage suffered by the immune system during the corona infection.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/delhi/be-alert-but-dont-panic-if-platelets-low-after-covid/articleshow/84303078.cms||Durgesh Nandan Jha

---||Delhi||Rs 51.7 crore: Covid fine Delhi paid in 2 months||NEW DELHI: If you had to put a figure to crass indiscipline, it would be 51.7 crore. That is the amount in rupees collected from careless Delhiites between April 23 and July 7 for disregarding Covid-appropriate behaviour. On April 20, Delhi reported over 28,000 single-day Covid cases and for many days patients were unable to find beds in hospitals or gasped for breath as oxygen supplies ran short, while the cremation grounds staggered with too many bodies to handle. But that apocalyptic ambience seems to have been quickly forgotten. After April 23, 2.7 lakh citizens have been penalised for disregarding the necessity to wear a mask. Over 27,000 people have been fined for not maintaining the required physical distancing in public, over 11,000 for spitting in the open, and over 3,000 for chewing gutka and tobacco or imbibing liquor in public spaces. An enforcement official said that most of the bookings took place in slightly over a month beginning with June when the government started lifting the lockdown restrictions in a phased manner and the number of people in public places started increasing. The lockdown relaxation began on May 31 with the government permitting manufacturing units in industrial areas and construction activities to restart. In phases after that, other commerce such as markets, malls, restaurants, gyms and yoga institutes were allowed to resume. Since the violations are dispersed across the city, the scale of violations has not been revealed, though the enforcement data indicates wide-spread, large-scale infractions. The volume of violations is alarming and shows that people do not bother about following the Covid guidelines despite the threat of a renewed surge. Since reopening, many crowded markets have seen blatant violations of the regulations about masks and social distancing, leading to a number of markets being closed by the district authorities. Chief minister Arvind Kejriwal has regularly appealed to Delhiites not to consider the Covid pandemic to be over, but to take care that the infection is checked by wearing masks and following social distancing norms. Delhi government has deployed 156 monitoring teams and around 130 vehicles to ensure strict enforcement of Covid norms across the city. At a Delhi Disaster Management Authority meeting on Friday, the 11 districts were asked to focus on enforcing the Covid regulations in public. Crowd-sensitive areas like markets, mandis, bus terminals, railway stations, restaurants are in the focus of the enforcement teams. The district authorities are also creating awareness among people by roping in market associations, residents welfare associations and other agencies. Dr Arun Gupta, president of Delhi Medical Council, said that similar irresponsible behaviour of the people was to a large extent responsible for the second Covid wave and continuing behaviour of this sort would usher in another spike in infections. ‚ÄúPeople must understand that the government alone cannot prevent Covid. It requires a collective effort and the citizens should adopt Covid-appropriate behaviour and also encourage others to do so,‚Äù said Gupta, who is also a member of Delhi government expert committee on the pandemic.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/delhi/rs-51-7cr-covid-fine-delhi-paid-in-2-mths/articleshow/84303043.cms||AlokKNMishra

---||Delhi||Delhi: From today, Mother Dairy milk goes up by Rs 2 per litre||NEW DELHI: After Amul, Mother Dairy has also decided to increase milk prices by Rs 2 per litre in Delhi-NCR and some other cities in the country. The new rates will come into effect from July 11. As per the revised prices, bulk vended milk (token milk) will be sold at Rs 44 per litre as against the current price of Rs 42 per litre. Full cream milk (poly pack) will now be available at Rs 57 per litre. The price of toned milk has been revised to Rs 47 and a litre of double toned milk will now cost Rs 41. The cow milk will cost Rs 49 per litre from Sunday.The standardised milk rates will now be Rs 51 per litre instead of Rs 49 per litre. The rates of half-litre milk pouch have been increased by Re 1. Super T milk pouches (500ml) will now be available for Rs 26. In a statement, Mother Dairy said, ‚ÄúThe company is compelled to raise its milk prices as it has been experiencing inflationary pressure on the overall input costs, which have increased multifold in the last one year. Despite paying higher prices towards milk procurement in the last one year, the consumer prices were kept intact. With this revision, the milk prices are undergoing a revision of 4%.‚Äù Apart from Delhi, milk prices are also being increased in other places like east and central Uttar Pradesh, Mumbai, Nagpur and Kolkata. Mother Dairy sells around 30 lakh litres of milk per day in Delhi-NCR, while the total sale is 35 lakh litres per day. ‚ÄúThe surge in farm prices is only being partially passed on to the consumers, thereby securing the interests of both the stakeholders,‚Äù the statement added. Mother Dairy stated that it passes close to 75-80 per cent of the sales realisation from milk towards the procurement of milk. ‚ÄúThe company believes in giving competitive and remunerative prices to the farmers to ensure sustainability of dairying and availability of safe milk for consumers.‚Äù The milk prices were last revised in December 2019. (DTIDC), an enterprise of the Delhi government that maintains and operates all ISBT‚Äôs and 1,397 bus queue shelters in the capital, is going to audit these facilities to create a barrier-free environment. The auditing is going to be carried out by an outside agency, following the Central Public Works Department‚Äôs handbook on a barrier-free environment and accessibility. The agency would prepare and submit the audit report within 60 days, for which Rs 7.5 lakh have been allotted. DTIDC said the audit will help identify the barriers that may exist at present, along with recommendations to overcome those. The audit team members will visit all the three ISBTs at Anand Vihar, Kashmere Gate and Sarai Kale Khan and all the 1,397 bus queue shelters maintained by DTIDC. The teams would take photographs and measurements of these facilities, which will be measured against the Indian standards on accessibility. The audit report will also take into consideration the needs of people with different disabilities and not merely locomotor impairments. An extensive audit report will be submitted to the engineer-in-charge at the end of the exercise. The primary areas that the audit teams would focus on at the ISBTs are the approach to the building premises, offices, ticket counters and windows, parking and drop off points, entrance, reception, help desk and visitor facilitation areas.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/delhi/isbts-bus-queue-shelters-to-turn-disabled-friendly/articleshow/84303217.cms||Sidharatha Roy

Interstate public and private transport and international air travel, except the ones permitted by the Union home ministry, however, will continue to remain prohibited. Curbs on cinema theatres, bars, swimming pools, social and political gatherings, entertainment, sports and cultural events, schools and colleges and zoological parks too will remain intact. A maximum of 50 people will be permitted to attend marriages, and 20 people for funerals and last rites. ‚ÄúAll permitted activities will be allowed to continue in the state, except in containment zones. Shops and other activities permitted till 8pm will be allowed till 9pm,‚Äù the CM said. Restaurants, tea shops, bakeries, eateries, sweet shops will be permitted with a 50% cap on customers at a time till 9pm. ‚ÄúStandard operating procedures should be followed strictly at all shops and public gatherings,‚Äù the CM said. Even as the total positive rate is falling, the state government wants to remain cautious. ‚ÄúThe state is still not in a comfort zone to open up fully,‚Äù said a senior official. Hand sanitizers and dispensers should be compulsorily made available at the entry and customers screened using thermal screening. Management should ensure that staff and customers wear masks at all times. Doors and windows should be kept open in shops with air-conditioning facilities to ensure adequate ventilation. Entry should be restricted to maintain social distance, while marking should be drawn for the customers to maintain distance when they stand in queue near shops. ‚ÄúThe district collectors and local bodies will have to take up intensive preventive measures through micro-level containment of cases,‚Äù he said. No other activities other than medical emergency services and supply of essential commodities will be permitted in the containment zones. The administrative machinery should set up committees and take up aggressive door-to-door monitoring in these zones. Stalin urged the public to avoid stepping out of houses and gather in public places to prevent the infectious disease. ‚ÄúWearing masks, maintaining social distance and frequent hand washing should be strictly followed. Public should visit hospitals nearby for consultation or treatment as soon as they get to know of the symptoms,‚Äù Stalin said. Imposing fines on violations of Covid protocols will continue, he said.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/chennai/govt-exams-bus-service-to-pondy-allowed-from-monday/articleshow/84303350.cms||---

---||Goa||Next wave possible if new variant emerges, say Goa experts||PANAJI: During the past fortnight, Goa‚Äôs Covid-19 graph seems to have plateaued at 150-250 cases, but the state may see a rise in August-September. It may not be substantial considering that a large section of the population will be vaccinated by then, provided that no new severe variant emerges. ‚ÄúIt appears that our cases have plateaued somewhere between 150 to 250 cases a day. Personally, if you ask me, even I‚Äôm waiting for these numbers to come down,‚Äù state epidemiologist Dr Utkarsh Betodkar said. Even though cases are low now, it is expected that in August and September there will be some activity in terms of cases increasing. ‚ÄúIt is difficult to say at this juncture the extent of the rise in cases that we may see. If people had not been vaccinated, I would say, the increase would be significant. But since our vaccination has gone very well, the potential increase in cases may not be high, but there shouldn‚Äôt be any new severe variant,‚Äù Betodakar said. He said it is not an easy task to predict what would be the scenario in the event any other new variant makes its way. So far, of the total of 120 samples tested to find out Covid variants ‚Äì since the beginning of the second wave ‚Äì 109 had delta strain, ten kappa and an alpha. The good part is, he said, the state conducts a large number of tests every day. On an average, 4,000 to 5,000 tests are done daily, including 1,000-1,500 at border check posts. The state‚Äôs case positivity rate has fallen below 5% over the past week ‚ÄúWe are not doing unnecessary tests. We are covering the target population even at border check posts,‚Äù he said. It‚Äôs mandatory for travellers coming to Goa that they either come with a Covid negative certificate or get tested at border check posts. Though places such as Margao, Ponda, Cortalim and Ponda have seen a gradual rise in cases in the last few days, he said, it may be because many members in a family testing positive. ‚ÄúSuppose, ten members in a family test positive, the case tally of the whole area goes up. Though a rise is seen in certain areas it is negligible. The ups and down noticed in the weekly average has been minimal,‚Äù he said. It is advisable that a weekly average is counted rather than a daily count. If an unusual rise is noticed it will be immediately brought to the notice of the government, he said.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/goa/next-wave-possible-if-new-variant-emerges/articleshow/84305278.cms||---
---||Dehradun||Dhami meets PM with request for new AIIMS in Kumaon||Dehradun: During his visit to the national capital as chief minister, Pushkar Singh Dhami met Prime Minister Narendra Modi on Saturday. Sources said that the meeting, initially scheduled for 15 minutes, lasted 75 minutes. Dhami requested the PM for an AIIMS ‚Äì on lines of the existing one at Rishikesh ‚Äì for the Kumaon region, as it would cater to a high number of people in the region. The CM is said to have told the PM that required land for such an institution was there, which can be immediately provided if the project is approved. Besides, Dhami told the PM that a sum of Rs 108 crore would be used for construction projects at Kedarnath, which would start shortly in the second phase of development process, and requested him to virtually lay foundation stones for these. The CM also requested the PM for the Cabinet Committee on Economic Affairs‚Äô approval for the Lakhwar Multipurpose Project. The Centre and six states - Uttar Pradesh, Delhi, Rajasthan, Haryana, Uttarakhand and Himachal Pradesh ‚Äì had signed an MoU in 2018 for the 300 MW hydropower plant on Yamuna so all these states could avert water crisis in the future. The project has got all approvals except that of the Cabinet Committee on Economic Affairs. Dhami said construction work will start on the project as soon as the approval is received. Afterwards, Dhami met Union home minister Amit Shah and requested to remove Niti Valley and Nelong Valley (Jadung village) of Uttarkashi from the inner line limits. The inner line permit (ILP) is a British-era system, under which outsiders visiting an area under the ILP will need permission from authorities and will be able to stay for a pre-specified time. The ILP is currently in force in northeastern states like Arunachal Pradesh, Nagaland and Mizoram. The CM also requested the home minister for permission to set up a Disaster Management Research Institute in Gairsain, for air ambulance facility in the state and for moving residents of disaster-affected villages under SDRF funds. He also sought permission for a provision on the local level to declare people missing in disasters as dead. He requested to split expenditure on central security forces deployed in the state during renowned fairs and occasions in a 90: 10 ratio, like it is done in north eastern and special category states. In view of limited financial resources of the state, the CM also requested for exemption of Rs 47.29 crore pending dues for the deployment of central security forces in the state from time to time. The CM urged to pay special attention to the situation of the hill states while preparing the guidelines for the State Disaster Risk Management Fund components. Dhami also met Union minister of housing and urban affairs Hardeep Puri and requested to increase the budget allocation of Uttarakhand from Rs 89 crore to Rs 150 crore for solid waste management projects under Swachh Bharat Mission-2. The CM urged to release the remaining share of the Centre for the processing and disposal schemes of 08 legacy waste and old dump sites of the seven municipal bodies of the state.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/dehradun/dhami-meets-pm-with-request-for-new-aiims-in-kumaon/articleshow/84301711.cms||Kautilya Singh

---||Mumbai||Rs 750-crore bank loans to sugar mill linked to Maharashtra deputy CM Ajit Pawar under ED lens||MUMBAI: Loans amounting to Rs 750 crore given by four cooperative banks to a sugar mill taken on lease by a company linked to deputy chief minister Ajit Pawar and his wife, Sunetra, have come under the scanner of the Enforcement Directorate during its investigation into a money laundering case. The ED has issued notices to the four banks, including Pune District Central Co-op Bank Ltd, where Pawar was a director. The ED is investigating the Rs 750 crore loan granted by the banks to Jarandeshwar Sahakari Sugar Karkhana (Jarandeshwar SSK). The Jarandeshwar SSK was purchased by Guru Commodity Services Pvt Ltd. It immediately leased Jarandeshwar SSK to Jarandeshwar Sugar Mills Pvt Ltd. A part of the funds utilised towards purchase of the mill was received from Sparkling Soil Pvt Ltd, a company related to Pawar and his wife, the ED had said. The ED saidJarandeshwar Sugar Mills Pvt Ltd and Guru Commodity Services Pvt Ltd were only a proxy owner of Jarandeshwar SSK and actual control rested with Sparkling Soil Pvt Ltd. Within a month of leasing out the mill, the Pune District Central Cooperative Bank, in which Pawar was one of the directors, had sanctioned Rs 100 crore loan to Jarandeshwar SSK. After a span of a few years, an additional Rs 650 crore loan was granted to Jarandeshwar SSK by Pune DCCB and other banks. The ED is trying to trace the financial trail. The ED is investigating a money laundering case connected with the Maharashtra State Co-Op Bank (MSCB). It suspects the Rs 750 crore loans taken by Jarandeshwar SSK were diverted for purposes other than declared to the bank. It was alleged that MSCB officials sanctioned loans to sick sugar mills and on default auctioned the assets. It is suspected that the MSCB officials ensured that their relatives or close associates bought the assets at the auction at throwaway prices. The ED said that while a developer from the city, Omkar Group, had floated the Guru Commodity Services Pvt Ltd by contributing around Rs 29 crore, Rs 10 crore came from another city developer, Shivalik Ventures. The remaining money was arranged by the Pawar-controlled company to purchase the Jarandeshwar SSK for Rs 60 crore in 2010, the ED had said. The ED has attached Jarandeshwar SSK sugar mill and the attachment notice stated that the auction was carried out in a way that the same could be purchased at an undervalued price by Guru Commodity, which was allegedly a dummy company operated by the Omkar Group.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/mumbai/mumbai-rs-750cr-bank-loans-to-sugar-mill-linked-to-dy-cm-under-ed-lens/articleshow/84307133.cms||Vijay V Singh

---||Pune||Maharashtra allocated 1.15 crore Covid vaccine doses for month, wants 1.5 crore||PUNE: All 12 crore Covid vaccine doses for July have been distributed fairly among states (depending on population size) and demands for more will have to wait until supply improves, health ministry officials have said. ‚ÄúUttar Pradesh is followed by Maharashtra, Bihar and West Bengal in vaccine allocation,‚Äù an official from the ministry said. On Friday, Maharashtra deputy chief minister Ajit Pawar had said unless supply from the Centre improves, the state would not be able to streamline its vaccination programme. Maharashtra has been allocated 1.15 crore doses for July. It has asked for 1.5 crore doses. Officials in key state districts, including Pune, have said that their target of more than one lakh daily vaccinations completely depends on how much the central government sends. On a few days this week, drives at several civic run sites in Pune and Pimpri Chinchwad were impacted due to limited supply. The health ministry official, when asked about the state‚Äôs request, said any addition to its allocated supply will lead to gaps in supply and demand in other states. The official said, ‚ÄúGap in (vaccine) demand and supply is a global issue. Current vaccine manufacturers have increased their production by four times, but demand has gone up too. That's why we started with priority groups (health and frontline workers), followed by vulnerable groups and then moved on to 45-plus and 18-plus groups.‚Äù The official said the Centre is not doubting Maharashtra's ability to ramp up its vaccine drive, but is currently unable to send more doses as supplies are still limited. ‚ÄúA vaccine is a biological product and has to undergo the necessary checks before distribution. Even if states demand immediate supplies, these processes have to be carried out, which will delay the supply. Consistent quality of the supply has to be ensured and that takes time,‚Äù the official, who didn't wish to be named, said. He said that vaccine ‚Äúeagerness‚Äù has increased after the second wave, adding that production has been improved to match the new levels of demand. ‚ÄúVaccine production has been increased from 2.5 crore to 12 crore. Work is on on all fronts. We are also adding vaccines from more manufacturers. But all this will take time. By next month, we will see supply improving further,‚Äù the official said. Vaccines from foreign manufacturers Moderna and Pfizer are expected to land soon in the country. At least 30 crore doses of the Biological E jab are also part of the Centre's supply plan for the rest of the year. Other central officials also confirmed that the Union government is committed to allocating 50 crore doses till Julyend and 135 crore between August and December. Authorities are also expecting daily vaccinations in the country to increase from 50 lakh to a crore. India has administered over 7.7 crore Covid-19 vaccine doses since rolling out its revamped central vaccination policy on June 21, with an average of 51.6 lakh inoculations per day.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/pune/maharashtra-allocated-1-15cr-doses-for-month-wants-1-5cr/articleshow/84305345.cms||Nisha Nambiar
---||Rajkot||Date-to-riches stories inspire Banaskantha tillers||Palanpur: A progressive horticulture farmer‚Äôs tryst with tissue culture is reaping him riches literally with record earning of Rs 1 crore annually! Meet Anadabhai Bhimjibhai Patel of Budhanpur village of Tharad taluka in Banaskantha who has made his orchard of fruits a sweet journey of farming excellence. Together with the know-how provided by Dantiwada Sardar Krushi University (SDAU), and of course, Patel‚Äôs own enthusiasm makes him a classic example of how a tiller can combine improvisation with initiative and make it a revolutionized wonder. ‚ÄúAnadabhai owns 64 bighas (40 acres) of farmland on which he grows pomegranate, papaya, ‚Äúapple ber‚Äù and ‚Äòkharek‚Äô or the Israeli dates. ‚ÄúA date plant sapling costs Patel Rs 3,800, of which, he gets a subsidy of Rs 1,250 from the state government. His overall earnings annually is more than Rs 1 crore,‚Äù Jignesh B Suthar, district horticulture officer told TOI.‚ÄúI have been getting earning consistently more than Rs 1 crore annually since 2017. We also engage about 15 labourers and their monthly remuneration totals to about Rs 2 lakh,‚Äù informed Patel. Patel‚Äôs scintillating annual turnover is a record of sorts in the horticulture area, as on an average Gujarat farmers earn around Rs 43,000 annually, which is why they are trapped in the vicious cycle of poverty. The turning point in his life had come when he wanted to grow other fruits too along with date through tissue culture in 2005. This type of tissue culture method of farming was introduced by scientists of SDAU, following a call given by Prime Minister Narendra Modi for self-sufficiency as the then state‚Äôs chief minister. Banaskantha horticulture division as well as SDAU provided Patel with more information that helped bring about a dramatic change in his outlook and he began to grow several fruits and flowers with spectacular results.Date farming needs a proper supply of water, for which Patel had made suitable arrangements in 2001 and has been holding him steady for all these years. Patel‚Äôs two brothers are also involved in date farming and all are happy with their progress. A date plant requires 4x3 feet pit and fertilisers like cowdung manure have to be added before planting a sapling. To save water, Patel uses drip irrigation which also reduces not only labour charges greatly, but also in consumption of water.What is special about Patel‚Äôs dates is that it is of Israeli variety and the whole process of growing it through organic farming has made it more beneficial for health. Patel has 300 date palms, of which, he first earned Rs 9 lakh. This steadily rose to Rs 15 lakh. Dates sell at Rs 60 to Rs 80 per kg in the market and Patel is now expecting a revenue of Rs 25 lakh from dates alone. Interestingly date farming can lead to intercrop farming which led Patel to also grow ‚Äúapple ber‚Äù, which has netted him an additional annual income of Rs 5 lakh.Such success stories have been a great inspiration for many more of his ilk in the Vav-Tharad area. Banaskantha, known for its potato cultivation primarily, is now turning into a hub for date farming thanks to the ingenuity and enterprise shown by farmers like Patel.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/rajkot/date-to-riches-stories-inspire-banaskantha-tillers/articleshow/84303437.cms||---

The report also found that 9.05% of all the schools in the state didn‚Äôt have a functional drinking water facility. But in a more worrying trend, the report highlighted that more than 16% of all schools in the state didn‚Äôt have an electricity connection. When it comes to the number of schools with internet facilities, only 16.67% of all schools in Uttarakhand are equipped with it, which means that more than 19,000 schools in the state are yet to be connected with the internet. On a national level, the internet was available in 22.3% of all schools in 2019-20. Just 8,000 schools have a functional computer facility, which means that more than 65% are yet to be equipped with computers. Nationally, 38.5% of all schools in India have computer facilities. ---||Rajkot||Mandatory hallmark leads to huge gold inventory pile-up across Gujarat||RAJKOT: After the new law, making hallmarking of gold jewellery compulsory from June 16 came into force, hallmarking centres across Gujarat have been facing a huge pile up of inventory. The government has fixed the August 1 deadline to get backlog stock to get hallmarked. Rajkot, the hub of lightweight gold jewellery design in the country, is especially facing the toughest challenges implementing the order owing to its lengthy procedure which has stalled supply to other states as well as abroad. The city manufactures around 40 kg gold jewellery every day. Industry sources claim that 80 percent jewellers in Rajkot never got their ornaments hallmarked earlier. Hallmark gold is a sign of trust. But in making the mark mandatory, the labyrinthine process is proving to be very cumbersome for the jewellers. Estimates suggest that in a day, barely 10% of the orders are processed. ‚ÄúEarlier, we used to process an estimated 2,000 requests in a day, but now we barely manage some 150 orders,‚Äù said a well-placed source working with a hallmarking centre. Earlier, the centre had to randomly check gold carat from 10% articles in one lot. But now, they have to generate a six digit HUID (hallmark unique identification number) for each article from a BIS portal. ‚ÄúThe entire method of inspecting has gone online. We must upload all details like weight, volume, type of gold used, grammage and other information online on the BIS server. We cannot release it till we get the HUID number, which is taking time. As a consequence, there is significant piling up of gold at the hallmarking centres,‚Äù said the source. Bhayabhai Soni, who runs the biggest hallmark centre in Rajkot, said, ‚ÄúWe have to upload every detail on the portal and create job cards. We have to generate a minimum 400 mg scrap of one lot of jewellery and mention that detail too. The entire process takes nearly two hours and in one day we can hallmark only 50 pieces.‚Äù Soni, who is also president of Rajkot gold dealers association, further said that server problems add to the long hours. According to a rough estimate around 70 to 100 kg gold ornaments lie piled up waiting to get a hallmark in Rajkot. Industry associations seek ease in compliance of norms for hallmarking jewellery. Ramesh Lolaria, a consultant of jewellers on hallmark issues said, ‚ÄúWe have suggested to the government to take a declaration from the traders of stock before June 16 and allow these to be sold without a hallmark. This will clear the huge backlog and waiting period.‚Äù Divyesh Patadiya, president of Rajkot gems and jewellery association said, ‚ÄúBecause of this waiting period, we have to make advance planning so that we can deliver ornaments to customers for marriage or festival which requires huge investment. Small traders can‚Äôt afford such investments.‚Äù Jitendra Bhindi, a Junagadh jeweller who was part of the committee on hallmarking, said that the government is positive in addressing all the problems. ‚ÄúHUIN is definitely a serious issue and the government has already formed a separate committee to find a solution to that issue,‚Äù he said. (With inputs from Niyati Parikh in Ahmedabad)||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/rajkot/mandatory-hallmark-leads-to-huge-gold-inventory-pileup/articleshow/84303503.cms||Nimesh Khakhariya

In contrast, Delhi, where the second wave saw the daily caseload soar to 25,000-plus, has seen 817 cases between July 1 and 10. Many major cities have a two-digit daily tally. There is no scientific answer yet as to why Maharashtra and Kerala continue to post a high number of cases almost six months into the second wave, but theories abound. Public health officials in the two states say the high numbers are a testimony of their transparent system and accurate reporting. One theory is that these numbers indicate a ‚Äúblip‚Äù in the second wave. ‚ÄúThese states reported the first cases/clusters in the country during both peaks. The high cases now could indicate another rise in the Covid graph,‚Äù said a senior doctor from Mumbai who didn‚Äôt want to be identified. In Maharashtra, doctors point to the curious case of Kolhapur, where the second wave has possibly just peaked with daily cases over 3,000 for the last fortnight as against under 800 in Mumbai. ‚ÄúWe have begun referring to this district as the ‚ÄòKolhapur paradox‚Äô,‚Äù said Dr Shashank Joshi, a member of the state government‚Äôs task force on Covid-19. ‚ÄúIt has the highest vaccinated percentage of 70% in the entire state, but it has the highest daily test positivity of over 10%,‚Äù said Dr Joshi. The Kolhapur cases, according to officials, are being reported among younger people who haven‚Äôt been fully vaccinated yet. Epidemiologist Dr Giridhar Babu said both Kerala and Maharashtra have different reasons for their high numbers. ‚ÄúThere is an issue with home isolation in Kerala. People in isolation are spreading it to others at home,‚Äù he said. But the fact that Kerala has low hospitalisation rates and low deaths ‚Äì 1,254 between July 1 and 10 as against 3,089 in Maharashtra ‚Äì indicates awareness about reaching out for healthcare in time. ‚ÄúKerala also has better immunisation rates,‚Äù he said. Regarding Maharashtra, he said various districts have witnessed peaks at different times. The real concern, he said, is that higher numbers indicate the virus is very much in circulation. Maharashtra state officials said July cases so far have dropped to the pre-peak levels in March. The peak-time daily average of 60,000 cases has reduced to a tenth, but the plateau has the government worried. ‚ÄúThere are eight districts that continue to be a cause for concern,‚Äù said a state official.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/mumbai/blip-in-2nd-wave-maharashtra-caseload-in-first-10-days-of-july-over-79500/articleshow/84305517.cms||Malathy Iyer

May be education can help them, he thought. In an attempt to educate the next generation of Bharwads, Jograna has opened a small chain of rural schools with his own might. The schools run right near the herdsmen‚Äô settlements, with teachers also settled close by. After starting with one school at Sonkhamb village in Nagpur‚Äôs Katol tehsil, he is set to open three more at villages in Umred, Hingna ana Saoner. The schools will be inaugurated on July 12. The schools have an arrangement with city NGO Learning Companion, where young persons interested to take up a career in education are engaged. The teachers, who come from different parts of the region, stay close to the schools, making themselves available on a daily basis. At present, the classes are from pre-primary to grade 4 and located close to different Bharwad settlements. The Bharwads may have given up their nomadic way of life, but even now they are settled away from the villages. ‚ÄúWe do have government schools in the villages but somehow the kids could not grasp the studies, may be the teachers are not very keen. The parents too, who are not educated, cannot assist them at home. I always wondered if some special arrangement could be made for our children,‚Äù said Jograna. ‚ÄúI finally got in touch with this NGO and they helped me start the schools. They are coming up at Badpipla in Saoner, Kuhiphata near Urmred and Asola village in Hingna. The teachers are local but have a different approach that suits us,‚Äù he says. Jograna also meets the day to day expenses of the teachers as they stay in the village itself. Jograna never missed a chance to discuss the problem with anyone resourceful he came across. Sajal Kulkarni, an activist who works with herdsmen, introduced him to the NGO. ‚ÄúWe have a system of training people who want to take up career in education. The NGO offers them a fellowship. The teachers are from different parts of the region who stay close to the community,‚Äù said Ganesh Birajdar of Learning Companion. The model not only provides exposure to the fellows but an opportunity to learn for the community members. Funding for the schools was raised through CSR activities of different companies. ‚ÄúJograna was keen to start the project and he approached us and we helped connect the dots,‚Äù said Prajakta Atul, one of the contributors. ‚ÄúThe children can speak broken Marathi but are comfortable with Hindi, which is also the medium of education. I have noticed that a number of children are rather good at mathematics. Their exposure to the bigger world is slowly increasing,‚Äù says Vrushab Khadse, a teacher who has already spent some time at the school in Sonkhambh. Jograna‚Äôs 17-year-old nephew Kalu is also keen to learn now. ‚ÄúSince we have a school here, we also take out time to learn to read and write,‚Äù he said Apart from education, Jograna says the community in Maharasthra also needs to get other basic facilities like Aadhaar cards.||http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com//city/nagpur/a-step-in-the-right-direction-this-herdsman-is-flocking-kids-to-school/articleshow/84301924.cms||Shishir Arya

---||Goa||Paediatric infra ready at South Goa district hospital||PANAJI: The paediatric unit to cater to the expected third wave of Covid has been readied at South Goa district hospital (SGDH), Margao. The last of the equipment that was to be installed was completed on Saturday. The unit, an 80-bed space, comprises 61 beds in the pediatric ward. It also has a seven-bed high dependency unit (HDU) with a separate space for children, including those with seizures who have to be remotely monitored where each bed has a monitor and HFNO and ventilator backup. A special newborn care unit (SNCU) has been fully equipped with twelve infant radiant warmers for new borns, most of which were donated by Verna industries association. The association has also donated other equipment to the hospital. The lobby of the second floor has been converted into a pediatric casualty where children can be assessed separately and won‚Äôt have to queue up with other people. Here the doctors will decide whether the child requires admission or not. The second wave initially saw people queueing up for hours outside casualty with no triage being carried out. ‚ÄúThe equipment has been installed and infrastructure is completely ready and functional. Under the POSH Act, a complaint is first assessed by an in-house or local mechanism ‚Äî a panel that also has a member from an NGO. The woman approached HC last year with a grievance that since the in-house panel informed her ‚Äúno action was required‚Äù on her complaint alleging sexual harassment, thereby dismissing it, she had nowhere to turn to. She also questioned her subsequent ‚Äúillegal termination‚Äù in June 2020. The company opposed her petition and also questioned its maintainability. At a hearing on March 11, the state had said the POSH Act provides for appeals against the IC report. The HC had directed the state to give details of whether such an appellate authority was set up. On July 8, the state informed the HC of its March 31 notification. ---||India||Unfazed by spinal fractures, ex-Navy man eyes rare feat||PANAJI: Undeterred by the horrific accident in 2018 that left him with two spinal fractures, former naval officer Abhilash Tomy is ready to cast off for another shot at circumnavigating the globe alone.
